Spiritual Beings as Causes of Events
Philosophers argue for eternal spiritual beings distinct from God as causes of events.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the philosophers' argument that the changing nature of events in the world requires a cause that itself changes, and that this cause must be an eternal spiritual being distinct from the unchanging God.

Core Idea
Changing events point to a changing cause, which cannot be the unchanging God.

In this passage, the philosophers present a key argument for the existence of spiritual beings (arwah) as the direct causes of events in this world. They reason that since events are constantly changing, their cause must also be subject to change, which cannot be God, who is absolutely unchanging. This leads to the conclusion that there must be high spirits that govern worldly phenomena.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the English translation to get the full sense of the argument.
Notice that the passage opens by stating a division of events into two kinds.
2
Identify the first division
The passage focuses on the first division: events caused by a spiritual being that transitions between intelligibles and perceptions. Note the description of this being as constantly moving from one perception to another.
3
Understand the distinction from God
The argument claims that this spiritual being must be eternal and distinct from God. Why? Because God is necessary in all aspects and thus unchanging, while this being undergoes change. Identify the reasoning that 'change is impossible for Him'.
This step is crucial for the argument.
4
Grasp the conclusion
The passage concludes that high spirits (arwah 'aliyah) are necessary as administrators of the world, and any extraordinary event requires their aid. Reflect on how this conclusion follows from the premises.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم نقول : هذه الحوادث تحتمل قسمين : أحدهما : أن يحصل في الوجود، موجود روحاني ، ويكون دائماً منتقلاً من معقول إلى معقول آخر، ومن إدراك إلى إدراك ، وبحسب تلك الإدراكات المتعاقبة ، والتصورات المتلاصقة، تحدث في هذا العالم . ويجب أن يكون الموجود الروحاني أزلياً أبدياً سرمدياً ، ويجب أن يكون شيئاً غير الله تعالى . لما ثبت واجب الوجود لذاته : واجب الوجود من جميع جهاته . فيكون التغير عليه محالاً ، فصاحب هذه الإدراكات المتغيرة : شيء غير الله تعالى . فقد ثبت : أن القول بوجود أرواح عالية ، هي المدبرة لأحوال هذا العالم لابد منه وبهذا الطريق فلا يتم السعي في إحداث شيء غريب في هذا العالم ، إلا بالاستعانة بتلك الأرواح .
Then we say: These events admit of two divisions: One of them: that there comes into existence a spiritual being, constantly moving from one intelligible to another, and from one perception to another, and according to those successive perceptions and contiguous conceptions, events occur in this world. And that spiritual being must be eternal, everlasting, perpetual, and it must be something other than God Most High. Because it is established that the Necessary Existence in Itself is Necessary Existence in all aspects. So change is impossible for Him, so the possessor of these changing perceptions is something other than God. So it is established that the assertion of the existence of high spirits, which are the administrators of the states of this world, is necessary, and in this way, the endeavor to produce something strange in this world is only accomplished by seeking the aid of those spirits.
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This passage presents the first possible explanation for the causes of events: a spiritual being that transitions between intelligibles and perceptions, and through these successive states, events are produced. This spiritual being must be eternal and distinct from God, because God (the Necessary Existent) is unchanging in all respects, whereas this being undergoes change. Therefore, the existence of high spirits that govern the world is necessary. Any attempt to produce extraordinary events must rely on these spirits.

معقول
إدراك
أزلي
أرواح عالية
مدبرة

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The spiritual being is God or another divine entity.
Correction: The argument explicitly states that this being is other than God because God is unchanging, while this being undergoes change.

Checkpoint

B) Because it is eternal like God

Key Takeaway

Why Perpetual Motion Must Be Circular
Philosophers argue that perpetual motion must be circular, not rectilinear.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the philosophical argument that perpetual physical motion, if it exists, must be circular rather than rectilinear.

Core Idea
Rectilinear motion cannot be perpetual because it requires either infinite dimensions or a moment of rest.

This passage from al-Matalib al-Aliyah presents a key argument from the philosophers: why a perpetual physical motion cannot be rectilinear. The argument uses a disjunction: either rectilinear motion extends infinitely or it returns. Both possibilities lead to absurdities or break perpetuity. Thus, only circular motion remains as a candidate for perpetual motion.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Carefully read the Arabic text and its English translation. Notice how the author sets up the disjunction and then eliminates the rectilinear option.
The text cuts off mid-sentence, but the logical conclusion is clear.
2
Identify the two possibilities for rectilinear motion
The passage says rectilinear motion either extends infinitely or it returns (reverses direction). Identify these two sub-cases.
3
Understand the infinite extension argument
If rectilinear motion extends infinitely, it would require infinite spatial dimensions, which is impossible. This is a key absurdity.
This is a reductio ad absurdum.
4
Understand the return argument
If rectilinear motion reverses direction, there must be a moment of rest between the forward and backward movements, breaking continuity. So the motion would not be perpetual.
5
Conclude the necessity of circular motion
Since both possibilities for rectilinear motion are impossible for perpetuity, the only remaining option is circular motion, which can be continuous without rest or infinite dimensions.
The passage leaves this conclusion implicit, but it is logically forced.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما القسم الثاني : وهو أن تحصل حركة جسمانية سرمدية دائمة ، مبرأة عن المبدأ والمقطع . فنقول : تلك الحركة إما أن تكون مستقيمة أو مستديرة ، والأول باطل لأن تلك الحركة إما أن تمتد إلى غير النهاية ، فيلزم وجود أبعاد لا نهاية لها ، وهو محال ، وإما أن ترجع ، وحينئذ يحصل بين نهاية الذهاب وبداية الرجوع : سكون لما ثبت أنه لابد وأن يكون بين كل حركتين من سكون ، وحينئذ لا تكون هذه الحركة دائمة ، مبرأة عن الانقطاع . فثبت أن كل حركة على الاستقامة ، فإنها تنقطع. فوجب : أن تكون كل
As for the second division: that a perpetual, everlasting, continuous physical motion occurs, free from beginning and termination. We say: That motion is either rectilinear or circular. The first is invalid because that motion either extends to infinity, necessitating infinite dimensions, which is impossible, or it returns, and then between the end of the going and the beginning of the returning occurs a rest, since it is established that between every two motions there must be a rest. Then this motion would not be perpetual, free from interruption. So it is established that every rectilinear motion is interrupted. Therefore, every [motion] must be...
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This passage presents the second possible cause: a perpetual physical motion. The argument tests whether such motion can be rectilinear or circular. Rectilinear motion is shown to be impossible because if it continues infinitely, it would require infinite dimensions (absurd), and if it reverses direction, there must be a moment of rest between the forward and backward movement, breaking perpetuity. Thus, rectilinear motion is necessarily interrupted. The conclusion, though cut off, is that the only possible perpetual motion is circular motion, which can continue without beginning or end and without inherent discontinuity.

Misconception: The argument proves that circular motion actually exists in the world.
Correction: The argument only shows that if a perpetual motion exists, it must be circular. It does not prove the existence of such motion.

Key Takeaway
Perpetual motion cannot be rectilinear because it would require infinite dimensions or a moment of rest, leaving circular motion as the only consistent possibility.

?

Proof that Celestial Motion is Circular and the First Proximate Cause
Argument proving circular motion as the only possible perpetual motion and first proximate cause.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational argument that perpetual physical motion must be circular, and why this is considered the first proximate cause of events in this world according to the philosophers.

Core Idea
Perpetual physical motion cannot be rectilinear; it must be circular, making it the proximate cause of all change.

In this passage, the author presents a key argument within Islamic philosophical theology: what kind of motion can serve as the immediate physical cause of events in the world? He considers two possibilities — rectilinear and circular — and demonstrates that only circular motion can be perpetual. This leads to the identification of the circular motion of celestial spheres as the first proximate cause. The passage then adds a further philosophical refinement, combining the physical and spiritual aspects.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the author uses a logical dichotomy and a disjunctive refutation.
2
Understand the dichotomy
The author assumes a perpetual physical motion exists and divides it into two possibilities: rectilinear or circular. This sets up the argument.
The dichotomy is exhaustive: any motion must be one of these two types.
3
Follow the refutation of rectilinear motion
Rectilinear motion is shown to be impossible because it either extends infinitely (impossible due to infinite dimensions) or turns back, requiring rest and breaking perpetuity.
This is a disjunctive syllogism: both options lead to impossibility, so the premise is false.
4
Grasp the conclusion
Since rectilinear motion is ruled out, the only remaining possibility is circular motion. Therefore, the perpetual motion must be circular, and that circular motion is the first proximate cause of events in the world.
The conclusion is not just about motion but about causation.
5
Consider the philosophical addition
The author adds that the philosophers combine both divisions: the celestial sphere as a body and its spiritual substance as a soul whose intellections cause motion. This refines the causal model.
This integrates the physical and spiritual aspects of the cause.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما القسم الثاني: وهو أن تحصل حركة جسمانية سرمدية دائمة، مبرأة عن المبدأ والمقطع. فنقول: تلك الحركة إما أن تكون مستقيمة أو مستديرة، والأول باطل لأن تلك الحركة إما أن تمتد إلى غير النهاية، فيلزم وجود أبعاد لا نهاية لها، وهو محال، وإما أن ترجع، وحينئذ يحصل بين نهاية الذهاب وبداية الرجوع: سكون لما ثبت أنه لابد وأن يكون بين كل حركتين من سكون، وحينئذ لا تكون هذه الحركة دائمة مبرأة عن الانقطاع. فثبت أن كل حركة على الاستقامة فإنها تنقطع. فوجب: أن تكون كل حركة مستديرة. وذلك يدل على أن المبدأ الأول القريب لحدوث الحوادث في هذا العالم: هو الحركة المستديرة الحاصلة للأجرام الفلكية. ثم قالت الفلاسفة: الأولى أن يجمع بين القسم الأول والثاني، حتى يكون جوهر الفلك كالبدن وجوهر ذلك الروح كالنفس، والتعقلات المنتقلة الدائمة لذلك الجوهر الروحاني توجب الحركات لهذه الكرات الجسمانية، ويكون مجموعها أسباباً لحدوث الحوادث في هذا العالم.
As for the second division: that there occurs a perpetual everlasting physical motion, free from beginning and end. We say: that motion is either rectilinear or circular, and the first is invalid because that motion either extends to infinity, which necessitates the existence of infinite dimensions, and that is impossible; or it turns back, and then between the end of the going and the beginning of the return there occurs rest, because it has been established that necessarily between every two motions there is rest, and then this motion would not be perpetual, free from interruption. So it is established that every rectilinear motion is interrupted. Therefore it is necessary that every motion be circular. And that indicates that the first proximate principle of the occurrence of events in this world is the circular motion occurring to the celestial bodies. Then the philosophers said: it is better to combine the first and second divisions, so that the substance of the sphere is like the body and the substance of that spirit is like the soul, and the perpetual transferring intellections of that spiritual substance necessitate the motions of these corporeal spheres, and their totality constitutes causes for the occurrence of events in this world.
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This passage presents the second type of cause: a perpetual physical motion without beginning or end. The author argues that such motion cannot be rectilinear because if it extended infinitely, it would require infinite spatial dimensions (impossible). If it reversed direction, there would necessarily be a rest between the forward and backward motions, breaking perpetuity. Therefore, the motion must be circular. This leads to the conclusion that the first proximate cause of events in the world is the circular motion of celestial spheres. The philosophers then add that it is better to combine both spiritual and physical aspects: the celestial body as a body and the spirit as its soul, with the spirit's continuous thoughts causing the motions, and together they are the causes of events.

Key Terms
حركة مستقيمة
حركة مستديرة
أبعاد لا نهاية لها
المبدأ الأول القريب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This argument proves that an eternal physical motion exists independent of God, implying that the universe has no Creator.
Correction: The argument is about the proximate cause within the world, not the ultimate cause. The philosophers still affirm God as the first cause, with the celestial motion being the immediate physical cause.

Checkpoint
Why does the author say that rectilinear motion cannot be perpetual?
A) Because it would require a beginning.
B) Because it would either lead to infinite dimensions or require rest when turning back, both breaking perpetuity.
C) Because only circular motion can be eternal.
D) Because rectilinear motion is less perfect.

Key Takeaway
This passage uses logical disjunction to prove that only circular motion can be perpetual, thereby establishing it as the first proximate cause of all events in the sublunary world.

?

Refutation of an Eternal Cause Without a Condition
Argument that an eternal cause without a temporal condition leads to impossibility, requiring a temporal condition and leading to infinite regress, concluding with circular motion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why an eternal cause cannot directly produce temporal events without a temporal condition, and how this leads to the conclusion that events are tied to circular celestial motion.

Core Idea
An eternal cause requires a temporal condition to produce a temporal effect, or the effect would be eternal.

This passage tackles a key problem in Islamic theology: how can an eternal God create temporal events? The author argues that an eternal cause without a temporal condition would make the effect eternal, which is impossible. If a condition is required, an infinite regress follows. The solution points to the endless circular motion of the heavens as the immediate cause of temporal events.

Guided Path
1
Understand the dilemma
Recognize the core problem: how can an eternal cause produce a temporal effect? The passage presents two possibilities and shows both lead to contradictions unless a special explanation is accepted.
The dilemma is between an immediate eternal effect (impossible) and an infinite chain of conditions (also problematic).
2
Analyze the two possibilities
Read the passage carefully and identify the two cases: (1) no temporal condition → effect would be eternal, (2) temporal condition → infinite regress. Note how each is refuted.
The author uses the same reasoning as in the first division (previous lesson).
3
Grasp the resolution
The conclusion asserts that temporal events are dependent on the circular motion of the celestial spheres, which is perpetual and uninterrupted, thus avoiding both problems.
This conclusion affirms a secondary cause that is itself eternal in its motion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما القسم الثاني: وهو أن يقال: السبب المقتضي لحدوث هذه الحوادث موجود قديم أزلي. فنقول: تأثير ذلك الأزلي في حدوث الحوادث إن كان غير موقوف على شرط حادث فهو محال، وإلا لزم كون هذا الحادث قديماً. وإن كان موقوفاً على شرط حادث عاد الكلام في كيفية حدوث ذلك الشرط الحادث، ويلزم التسلسل، ويعود جملة ما ذكرناه في القسم الأول. فيثبت بهذا البيان: أن حدوث الحوادث في هذا العالم منوطة ومربوطة بالحركة المستديرة الفلكية المبرأة عن الانقطاع والتغير.
As for the second division: that it is said: the cause necessitating the occurrence of these events is an ancient eternal existent. We say: the effect of that eternal in the occurrence of events, if it is not dependent on a temporal condition, then it is impossible, otherwise it would necessitate that this temporal event be eternal. And if it is dependent on a temporal condition, then the discussion returns to the manner of occurrence of that temporal condition, and an infinite regress follows, and the entirety of what we mentioned in the first division returns. So by this explanation it is established: that the occurrence of events in this world is dependent and tied to the circular celestial motion that is free from interruption and change.
Source pages p. 152

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the claim that an eternal cause could directly produce temporal events without any condition. The author argues that if the eternal cause's effect is not conditional on a temporal event, then the effect would be eternal (since the cause is eternal), but events are temporal, so this is impossible. If it is conditional on a temporal event, then that condition itself needs a cause, leading to an infinite regress, which is the same problem as before. Therefore, the only way to avoid this is to accept that events are produced by the circular motion of the celestial spheres, which is perpetual and without interruption.

Key Terms
سبب قديم أزلي
شرط حادث
تسلسل
حركة مستديرة فلكية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The argument denies God's power to create directly.
Correction: The argument does not deny God's power; it demonstrates that an eternal cause logically requires a temporal condition to produce a temporal effect, otherwise the effect would be eternal. This does not limit God's power but explains the necessity of secondary causes like celestial motion.

Checkpoint
What is the conclusion of the argument about an eternal cause producing events?
A) The eternal cause can produce events directly.
B) The eternal cause must have a temporal condition, leading to infinite regress, so events must be tied to circular motion.
C) The eternal cause is impossible.
D) The events are uncaused.

Key Takeaway
Temporal events cannot be directly caused by an eternal cause without a temporal condition; the only coherent explanation is that they are mediated by the perpetual circular motion of the heavens.

From Uniform Spheres to Diverse Bodies
Proof that diversity of earthly events requires diverse celestial bodies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the observed diversity of events in the sublunary world necessitates the existence of diverse celestial bodies with different motions.

Core Idea
Diversity below proves diversity above.

This passage presents a logical argument from observed effect to necessary cause. The author starts with the premise that the celestial spheres are simple and uniform, then shows that such uniformity would produce uniform earthly events. Since we observe diverse events (generation and corruption), there must be diversity in the celestial causes. We'll walk through this reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Carefully read the Arabic text and its literal translation. Understand the flow of the argument before analyzing its parts.
2
Identify the premise and conditional
Find the premise that celestial bodies are simple and similar. Then locate the conditional: if similar causes, then similar effects.
3
Observe the contradiction
The author states that events are not uniform but diverse. This contradicts the conditional consequence, so the premise must be modified.
The diversity of events is a given observable fact.
4
Trace the conclusion and implications
The conclusion: there must be diverse bodies in the celestial realm. Then note the further steps: these bodies move, their motions produce different relations, which are principles for diverse events below.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم نقول: الأجرام الفلكية بسائط، والأجزاء المفترضة في الكرة البسيطة متشابهة بالطبع والماهية، والأسباب المتماثلة في الطبع والماهية لا تفيد إلا معلومات متماثلة. فكان يجب أن تكون حوادث هذا العالم متساوية، وذلك باطل. ولما بطل هذا، وجب أن يحصل في الأجرام الفلكية أجسام مختلفة في الطبيعة والماهية. ولابد وأن تكون تلك الأشياء متحركة. ويحصل لها بسبب حركاتها المختلفة: نسب مختلفة، وتكون تلك النسب المختلفة مبادى لحدوث الحوادث المختلفة في عالم الكون والفساد.
Then we say: The celestial bodies are simple, and the assumed parts in the simple sphere are similar in nature and essence, and causes that are similar in nature and essence yield only similar effects. So it would be necessary that the events of this world be uniform, but that is false. And when this was invalidated, it became necessary that there come to be in the celestial bodies bodies different in nature and essence. And those things must be moving. And due to their different motions, different relations occur, and those different relations are principles for the occurrence of different events in the world of generation and corruption.
Source pages p. 152

Commentary
This passage is an argument from observed diversity. It starts from the premise that the celestial spheres are simple and uniform in nature. If they were entirely uniform, they would produce uniform effects in the sublunary world. But we observe diverse events (generation and corruption). Therefore, there must be within the celestial spheres bodies that are different in nature and essence. These bodies must be moving, and their different motions produce different relations, which are the principles of the diverse events in the sublunary world.

Key Terms
أجرام فلكية بسائط
طبع وماهية
نسب مختلفة
عالم الكون والفساد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The diversity of earthly events is due to random chance or inherent unpredictability.
Correction: The argument shows that diversity must be traced back to diverse causes in the celestial realm, not to randomness. The celestial bodies produce systematic relations that account for sublunary diversity.

Checkpoint
Why does the author argue that there must be different bodies in the celestial spheres?
A) Because the spheres are made of different elements.
B) Because if they were uniform, events would be uniform, but they are diverse.
C) Because the spheres move at different speeds.
D) Because the philosophers said so.

Key Takeaway
The diversity of events in the sublunary world proves that celestial spheres contain bodies of different natures and motions, which produce the varied phenomena we observe.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider the diversity in your own life—your changing circumstances, thoughts, and actions—do you attribute them to a single uniform cause like pure chance, or do you recognize, as this proof shows, that different effects require different causes? How does this awareness change your reliance on Allah as the ultimate cause of all causes?
?
This proof deduces that diversity in the heavenly motions produces diversity on earth. In your spiritual life, what 'motions'—your acts of worship, intentions, or daily routines—are producing the outcomes you see? Are there motions you need to change to produce different effects? What is one specific change you can make today?
?
The argument shows that uniformity would lead to monotony. Reflect on the diversity Allah has placed in creation and in your own experiences. What does this teach you about His wisdom and mercy? Does it increase your gratitude? How can you express that gratitude beyond words?

The Rational Proof of Celestial Motion as Proximate Cause
Al-Razi presents the first part of the rational proof on celestial motion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Razi's rational proof establishes that circular celestial motion is the proximate cause of all sublunar events.

Core Idea
Circular motion is the closest cause of all change in our world.

Al-Razi begins his exposition of the philosophers' proof by identifying the circular motion of celestial spheres as the first proximate principle for the occurrence of events. He then discusses two divisions to support this claim, ultimately showing that events are dependent on this motion. This lesson unpacks that initial argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyze it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the concise style of Al-Razi.
2
Identify the main claim
Find where Al-Razi states that circular motion is the first proximate principle for the occurrence of events.
It is at the very beginning: 'حركة مستديرة. وذلك يدل...'
3
Understand the two divisions
Al-Razi presents two divisions (القسم الأول والثاني) that support the claim. The first combines celestial sphere and spirit; the second deals with an eternal cause and temporal condition.
The second division uses an argument from impossibility of an eternal cause without temporal condition.
4
See the conclusion
Both divisions lead to the conclusion that events are dependent on circular celestial motion, which is free from interruption.
The conclusion is explicitly stated after the second division.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حركة مستديرة. وذلك يدل على أن المبدأ الأول القريب لحدوث الحوادث في هذا العالم: هو الحركة المستديرة الحاصلة للأجرام الفلكية. ثم قالت الفلاسفة: الأولى أن يجمع بين القسم الأول والثاني. حتى يكون جوهر الفلك، كالبدن وجوهر ذلك الروح كالنفس. والتعقلات المنتقلة الدائمة لذلك الجوهر الروحاني، توجب الحركات لهذه الكرات الجسمانية، ويكون مجموعها أسباباً لحدوث الحوادث في هذا العالم.
وأما القسم الثاني: وهو أن يقال: السبب المقتضي لحدوث هذه الحوادث موجود قديم أزلي. فنقول: تأثير ذلك الأزلي في حدوث الحوادث [إن كان غير موقوف على شرط حادث] فهو محال، وإلا لزم كون هذا الحادث قديماً وإن كان موقوفاً على شرط حادث [عاد الكلام في كيفية حدوث ذلك الشرط الحادث، ويلزم التسلسل، ويعود جملة ما ذكرناه في القسم الأول] فيثبت بهذا البيان: أن حدوث الحوادث في هذا العالم، منوطة ومربوطة بالحركة المستديرة الفلكية، المبرأة عن الانقطاع والتغير.
ثم نقول: الأجرام الفلكية بسائط، والأجزاء المفترضة في الكرة البسيطة؛ متشابهة بالطبع، والماهية [والأسباب المتماثلة في الطبع والماهية] لا تفيد إلا معلومات متماثلة. فكان يجب أن تكون حوادث هذا العالم متساوية، وذلك باطل. ولما بطل هذا، وجب أن يحصل في الأجرام الفلكية، أجسام مختلفة في الطبيعة والماهية. ولابد وأن تكون تلك الأشياء متحركة. ويحصل لها بسبب حركاتها المختلفة: نسب مختلفة، وتكون تلك النسب المختلفة، مبادى لحدوث [الحوادث المختلفة في عالم الكون والفساد] ومعلوم أن تلك الأجسام المختلفة المركوزة في جواهر الأفلاك ليست إلا الكواكب. فثبت بما ذكرنا: أن مبادىء الحوادث الحادثة في هذا العالم ليست إلا الاتصالات الكوكبية المختلفة. فهذا هو البرهان الذي عليه تعويل الفلاسفة في إثبات هذا المطلوب.
Circular motion. And that indicates that the first proximate principle for the occurrence of events in this world is the circular motion that occurs for the celestial bodies. Then the philosophers said: It is better to combine the first and second divisions. So that the substance of the celestial sphere is like the body, and the substance of that spirit is like the soul. And the perpetual transferred intellections for that spiritual substance necessitate motions for these corporeal spheres, and their totality becomes causes for the occurrence of events in this world. As for the second division: That it be said: The necessitating cause for the occurrence of these events is an eternal preexistent existent. We say: The effect of that eternal [cause] in the occurrence of events, if it is not conditional upon a temporal condition, it is impossible, otherwise this temporal would be eternal; and if it is conditional upon a temporal condition, the discussion returns to how that temporal condition occurs, and infinite regress follows, and the entirety of what we mentioned in the first division returns. So by this exposition it is established that the occurrence of events in this world is dependent and connected to the circular celestial motion, which is free from interruption and change. Then we say: The celestial bodies are simple, and the parts assumed in the simple sphere are similar in nature and essence. And causes that are similar in nature and essence do not produce except similar effects. So it would be necessary that the events of this world be equal, and that is false. And when this was invalidated, it became necessary that there exist in the celestial bodies differing bodies in nature and essence. And those things must be moving. And due to their different motions, different relationships occur for them, and those different relationships become principles for the occurrence of the different events in the world of generation and corruption. And it is known that those different bodies embedded in the substances of the celestial spheres are nothing but the planets. So it is established by what we have mentioned that the principles of the events occurring in this world are nothing but the different planetary conjunctions. This is the proof upon which the philosophers rely in establishing this sought conclusion.
Source pages p. 152

Commentary
This passage presents the rational proof (برهان) of the philosophers for the claim that the proximate cause of all events in the sublunar world is the circular motion of celestial bodies, specifically the planetary conjunctions. The proof begins by stating that circular motion is the first proximate principle. Then it discusses two possible divisions: the first combines the celestial sphere's substance as body and a spiritual substance as soul, with intellections causing motions; the second argues that an eternal cause acting without a temporal condition would make the effect eternal, so it must act upon a condition, which leads to regress unless that condition is the circular motion itself. Thus it is established that events are connected to circular motion. Then a second part refutes the objection that if celestial spheres are simple and uniform, their effects would be uniform, but we see diversity. Therefore there must be diverse bodies within the spheres, which are the planets, and their different motions produce different relationships (conjunctions), which are the principles of events. The proof concludes that planetary conjunctions are the only causes of events.

Key Terms

أجرام فلكية
برهان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The proof asserts that celestial spheres are intelligent agents.
Correction: The proof does not assert that celestial spheres are intelligent agents; rather, it argues that their motions are mechanical causes, though it uses an analogy with a soul to explain the relationship.

Checkpoint
What does Al-Razi identify as the first proximate principle for the occurrence of events in this world?
A) The spiritual substances
B) The circular motion of celestial bodies
C) The planetary conjunctions
D) The eternal cause

Key Takeaway
The rational proof establishes circular celestial motion as the proximate cause of all sublunar events.

?

?
The philosophers argued that celestial motion is free from interruption. Where in your own worship or character is there 'interruption'—inconsistency or neglect—that you need to align with that steady rhythm? What one change would make your obedience more constant like that motion?
?
This proof suggests that there is a precise, unbroken chain of causes leading to every event in your life. Does this comfort you or trouble you? Would trusting that every outcome has a determined cause make you more patient with delays and setbacks? What would you need to truly internalize this?

The Rational Proof of Planetary Conjunctions as Causes of Events
Al-Razi completes the rational proof by deducing planetary conjunctions as causes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the diversity of sublunar events leads to the conclusion that planetary conjunctions are their principles.

Core Idea
Diverse events require diverse causes, and those are the planetary conjunctions.

Having established the role of circular motion, Al-Razi addresses a potential objection: if celestial spheres are uniform, their effects should be uniform. Yet we observe diversity. This leads to the necessary conclusion that there must be diverse bodies within the spheres—the planets—and their different conjunctions cause the varied events in our world.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and translation carefully. Notice that this part starts with 'ثم نقول'.
This is the second part of the overall proof.
2
Understand the uniformity objection
Al-Razi states that celestial bodies are simple and uniform; uniform causes produce uniform effects, but events are diverse, so the assumption is false.
This is a reductio ad absurdum.
3
Identify the necessary conclusion
Because uniformity is false, there must be diverse bodies within the spheres. These bodies are identified as the planets.
The argument moves from diversity to the existence of planets.
4
Trace the final step
The planets' different motions produce different relationships (conjunctions), which become the principles of diverse events.
The proof concludes that planetary conjunctions are the only principles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حركة مستديرة. وذلك يدل على أن المبدأ الأول القريب لحدوث الحوادث في هذا العالم: هو الحركة المستديرة الحاصلة للأجرام الفلكية. ثم قالت الفلاسفة: الأولى أن يجمع بين القسم الأول والثاني. حتى يكون جوهر الفلك، كالبدن وجوهر ذلك الروح كالنفس. والتعقلات المنتقلة الدائمة لذلك الجوهر الروحاني، توجب الحركات لهذه الكرات الجسمانية، ويكون مجموعها أسباباً لحدوث الحوادث في هذا العالم.
وأما القسم الثاني: وهو أن يقال: السبب المقتضي لحدوث هذه الحوادث موجود قديم أزلي. فنقول: تأثير ذلك الأزلي في حدوث الحوادث [إن كان غير موقوف على شرط حادث] فهو محال، وإلا لزم كون هذا الحادث قديماً وإن كان موقوفاً على شرط حادث [عاد الكلام في كيفية حدوث ذلك الشرط الحادث، ويلزم التسلسل، ويعود جملة ما ذكرناه في القسم الأول] فيثبت بهذا البيان: أن حدوث الحوادث في هذا العالم، منوطة ومربوطة بالحركة المستديرة الفلكية، المبرأة عن الانقطاع والتغير.
ثم نقول: الأجرام الفلكية بسائط، والأجزاء المفترضة في الكرة البسيطة؛ متشابهة بالطبع، والماهية [والأسباب المتماثلة في الطبع والماهية] لا تفيد إلا معلومات متماثلة. فكان يجب أن تكون حوادث هذا العالم متساوية، وذلك باطل. ولما بطل هذا، وجب أن يحصل في الأجرام الفلكية، أجسام مختلفة في الطبيعة والماهية. ولابد وأن تكون تلك الأشياء متحركة. ويحصل لها بسبب حركاتها المختلفة: نسب مختلفة، وتكون تلك النسب المختلفة، مبادى لحدوث [الحوادث المختلفة في عالم الكون والفساد] ومعلوم أن تلك الأجسام المختلفة المركوزة في جواهر الأفلاك ليست إلا الكواكب. فثبت بما ذكرنا: أن مبادىء الحوادث الحادثة في هذا العالم ليست إلا الاتصالات الكوكبية المختلفة. فهذا هو البرهان الذي عليه تعويل الفلاسفة في إثبات هذا المطلوب.
Circular motion. And that indicates that the first proximate principle for the occurrence of events in this world is the circular motion that occurs for the celestial bodies. Then the philosophers said: It is better to combine the first and second divisions. So that the substance of the celestial sphere is like the body, and the substance of that spirit is like the soul. And the perpetual transferred intellections for that spiritual substance necessitate motions for these corporeal spheres, and their totality becomes causes for the occurrence of events in this world. As for the second division: That it be said: The necessitating cause for the occurrence of these events is an eternal preexistent existent. We say: The effect of that eternal [cause] in the occurrence of events, if it is not conditional upon a temporal condition, it is impossible, otherwise this temporal would be eternal; and if it is conditional upon a temporal condition, the discussion returns to how that temporal condition occurs, and infinite regress follows, and the entirety of what we mentioned in the first division returns. So by this exposition it is established that the occurrence of events in this world is dependent and connected to the circular celestial motion, which is free from interruption and change. Then we say: The celestial bodies are simple, and the parts assumed in the simple sphere are similar in nature and essence. And causes that are similar in nature and essence do not produce except similar effects. So it would be necessary that the events of this world be equal, and that is false. And when this was invalidated, it became necessary that there exist in the celestial bodies differing bodies in nature and essence. And those things must be moving. And due to their different motions, different relationships occur for them, and those different relationships become principles for the occurrence of the different events in the world of generation and corruption. And it is known that those different bodies embedded in the substances of the celestial spheres are nothing but the planets. So it is established by what we have mentioned that the principles of the events occurring in this world are nothing but the different planetary conjunctions. This is the proof upon which the philosophers rely in establishing this sought conclusion.

The proof begins by stating that circular motion is the first proximate principle. Thus it is established that events are connected to circular motion. The proof concludes that planetary conjunctions are the only causes of events.

The Inductive Argument for Astrology's Validity
Al-Razi presents the philosophers' inductive argument based on observed correlations and historical consensus on astrology.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two-pronged inductive argument used by philosophers to support astrology: empirical correlation and historical consensus.

Core Idea
Inductive reasoning from nature and history jointly supports astrology's claims.

Al-Razi presents the philosophers' inductive argument (حجة إقناعية), which does not prove astrology definitively but offers strong circumstantial evidence. The argument first points to observable connections between celestial motions and earthly seasons, then appeals to the universal historical practice of astrology. This lesson unpacks both components and their logical force.

Guided Path
1
Read the full passage carefully
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Get a sense of the overall argument before analyzing its parts.
Notice that Al-Razi uses the term 'حجة إقناعية' to label this as an inductive, not demonstrative, argument.
2
Identify the two parts of the argument
The passage has two clear sections: first, the empirical observation linking the sun's motion to seasons and earthly changes; second, the historical consensus that astrology has been practiced universally since ancient times.
Look for the phrase 'ثم تأكد هذا البيان بنوع آخر' which marks the transition.
3
Evaluate the strength of each part
Consider why Al-Razi calls this an 'inductive' (إقناعية) rather than a demonstrative argument. Each part relies on observed patterns and widespread acceptance, not logical necessity.
Inductive arguments are probabilistic; they increase likelihood but do not guarantee truth.
4
Reflect on the role of universal consensus
The philosophers argue that if astrology were false, it would not have been universally accepted across all cultures and times. Think about whether consensus alone is a reliable indicator of truth.
This echoes arguments used in other fields, such as the universal acceptance of certain moral principles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الحجة الثانية - وهي الحجة الإقناعية - فهي أنهم قالوا: إنا قد ذكرنا وجوهاً كثيرة دالة على أن أحوال هذا العالم، مرتبطة بأحوال الشمس في كيفية حركتها، تحت منطقة البروج، فإن بهذا السبب تصير الشمس تارة شمالية، وتارة جنوبية، ولأجل هذا الاختلاف تحصل الفصول الأربعة، ويسببها تختلف أحوال هذا العالم، [وأيضاً: بسبب طلوع الشمس وغروبها في اليوم، تختلف أحوال هذا العالم] وهذا استقراء قوي، وبيان تام في استناد أحوال هذا العالم بحركات الكواكب ثم تأكد هذا البيان بنوع آخر من البيان، وهو: أن الناس منذ كانوا من قديم الدهر، كانوا متمسكين بعلم النجوم ومعولين عليها. فإنك ترى لكل علم أولاً، وإنساناً هو أول الناس خوضاً فيه. إلا العلم الإلهي، وعلم النجوم، فإنك لا تصل إلى تاريخ، إلا وترى أن هذين العلمين كانا موجودين قبله، ولو كان هذا العلم باطلا، لامتنع إطباق أهل الدنيا من الدهر الداهر، إلى هذا اليوم، على التمسك به والرجوع إليه. فهذه الوجوه، بيانات ظاهرة في صحة هذا العلم [والله أعلم].
As for the second argument—and it is the inductive argument—it is that they said: We have mentioned many aspects indicating that the conditions of this world are connected to the conditions of the sun in terms of its motion under the zodiac; for by this cause the sun becomes sometimes northern and sometimes southern, and due to this difference the four seasons occur, and because of them the conditions of this world differ. [Also: due to the rising and setting of the sun during the day, the conditions of this world differ.] And this is a strong induction and a complete demonstration of the dependence of the conditions of this world on the motions of the planets. Then this demonstration was strengthened by another type of demonstration, which is: People since time immemorial have been adhering to astrology and relying upon it. For you see for every science a first [beginning] and a person who is the first to delve into it, except for theology and astrology; for you do not reach a date except that you see that these two sciences existed before it. And if this science were false, it would be impossible for the people of the world from eternal time until today to unanimously adhere to it and resort to it. These aspects are clear demonstrations of the correctness of this science. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This passage presents the inductive argument (حجة إقناعية) of the philosophers. It is not a strict demonstration but an approximate proof based on observation and historical consensus. First, they cite empirical correlations: the sun's motion causes seasons and daily variations, and by extension all planetary motions affect worldly conditions. This is a strong induction. Second, they note that astrology has been practiced universally since ancient times, unlike other sciences that have identifiable founders. The fact that all people throughout history have adhered to astrology is taken as evidence of its truth, for a false science would not receive such universal acceptance. Thus they argue for the validity of the connection between celestial motions and earthly events.

Key Terms
حجة إقناعية
استقراء
علم النجوم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the historical consensus argument is a rational proof, but it is actually an inductive argument.
Correction: Al-Razi explicitly labels this as a 'حجة إقناعية' (inductive argument), not a demonstrative one. Inductive arguments are based on observation and probability, not logical necessity.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The philosophers support astrology through inductive evidence: observed causal patterns in nature and the unbroken historical practice of astrology worldwide.

The Philosophers' Definitive Proof: Planetary Conjunctions as Causes
Presents the philosophers' definitive proof for planetary conjunctions as causes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the philosophers' definitive proof that planetary conjunctions are the sole cause of events in this world.

Core Idea
For the philosophers, planetary conjunctions are not coincidences—they are the principles of all events.

This lesson presents a key philosophical argument about causality. The philosophers claim that the bodies embedded in the celestial spheres are nothing but planets, and from this they deduce that all events in this world originate from planetary conjunctions. Let us examine this proof and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic text and its translation. Notice the deductive structure: a premise leading to a conclusion.
The philosophers rely on this as a definitive proof.
2
Analyze the proof's structure
Identify the premise (what are the bodies in the celestial spheres?) and the conclusion (what are the principles of events?). Reflect on why this might be controversial from a theological perspective.

أن تلك الأجسام المختلفة المركوزة في جواهر الأفلاك ليست إلا الكواكب . فثبت بما ذكرنا : أن مبادىء الحوادث الحادثة في هذا العالم ليست إلا الاتصالات الكوكبية المختلفة. فهذا هو البرهان الذي عليه تعويل الفلاسفة في إثبات هذا المطلوب

The passage then declares that this is the proof that the philosophers rely on to establish their claim. The argument proceeds deductively: since the celestial bodies are planets, and events correlate with their motions and conjunctions, the cause of events must be those conjunctions.

Persuasive Arguments for Astrology: Experience and Consensus
Presents two persuasive arguments: induction from seasons/daily changes and consensus of all people throughout history.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand two persuasive arguments used to support astrology: the inductive argument from observed correlations and the argument from universal historical consensus.

Core Idea
Two persuasive arguments support astrology: observed patterns and universal human agreement.

The philosophers present a second type of argument for astrology, which they call 'persuasive' (إقناعية). This argument does not claim logical necessity but relies on strong inductive evidence and the fact that all human societies have embraced astrology since ancient times. The passage below presents these two lines of reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the argument is presented as a follow-up to a previous one.
2
Identify the two sub-arguments
The passage contains two distinct lines of evidence: an inductive one based on the sun's motion and seasons, and a consensus argument based on universal historical adherence. Locate each one.
3
Reflect on persuasive vs. demonstrative
The passage calls this 'persuasive' (إقناعية). Why might the author not claim it is a logical proof? Think about the nature of induction and consensus as arguments.
This will help you understand the author's epistemological classification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الحجة الثانية - وهي الحجة الإقناعية - فهي أنهم قالوا : إنا قد ذكرنا وجوهاً كثيرة دالة على أن أحوال هذا العالم ، مرتبطة بأحوال الشمس في كيفية حركتها ، تحت منطقة البروج ، فإن بهذا السبب تصير الشمس تارة شمالية ، وتارة جنوبية ، ولأجل هذا الاختلاف تحصل الفصول الأربعة ، ويسببها تختلف أحوال هذا العالم ، وأيضاً : بسبب طلوع الشمس وغروبها في اليوم ، تختلف أحوال هذا العالم وهذا استقراء قوي ، وبيان تام في استناد أحوال هذا العالم بحركات الكواكب ثم تأكد هذا البيان بنوع آخر من البيان ، وهو : أن الناس منذ كانوا من قديم الدهر ، كانوا متمسكين بعلم النجوم ومعولين عليها . فإنك ترى لكل علم أولاً ، وإنساناً هو أول الناس خوضاً فيه . إلا العلم الإلهي ، وعلم النجوم ، فإنك لا تصل إلى تاريخ ، إلا وترى أن هذين العلمين كانا موجودين قبله ، ولو كان هذا العلم باطلا ، لامتنع إطباق أهل الدنيا من الدهر الداهر ، إلى هذا اليوم ، على التمسك به والرجوع إليه . فهذه الوجوه ، بيانات ظاهرة في صحة هذا العلم والله أعلم
And as for the second argument—which is the persuasive argument—it is that they said: We have indeed mentioned many aspects indicating that the states of this world are connected to the states of the sun in the manner of its motion under the zodiacal belt, for by this reason the sun becomes sometimes northern and sometimes southern, and due to this variation the four seasons occur, and by them the states of this world vary. Also, due to the rising and setting of the sun in the day, the states of this world vary. And this is a strong induction (استقراء قوي) and a complete demonstration of the dependence of the states of this world on the motions of the planets. Then this demonstration was confirmed by another type of demonstration, which is: that people since ancient times have been adhering to the science of the stars (علم النجوم) and relying upon it. For you see that every science has a founder, a first person who delved into it, except for the divine science (العلم الإلهي) and the science of the stars, for you do not come across any history except that you find these two sciences existed before it. And if this science were false, it would be impossible for the people of the world from time immemorial to this day to unanimously adhere to it and refer to it. These aspects are clear proofs of the soundness of this science—and God knows best.
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This passage presents the persuasive argument (الحجة الإقناعية) of the philosophers. It consists of two main parts. First, an inductive argument (استقراء) based on observed correlations: the sun's movement under the zodiac causes seasons and daily changes, affecting worldly states. This is presented as strong induction and a complete demonstration (بيان تام) of the dependence of earthly states on planetary motions. Second, an argument from universal consensus: from ancient times, all people have adhered to astrology (علم النجوم) and relied upon it. The author notes that unlike other sciences which have known founders, astrology and divine science (العلم الإلهي) are found in all historical records without a known originator. The conclusion is that if astrology were false, it would be impossible for all people throughout history to unanimously accept it. Thus these are presented as clear proofs of the science's validity.

Key Terms
الحجة الإقناعية
الاستقراء
علم النجوم
الإجماع
منطقة البروج
الفصول الأربعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The argument from consensus is a logical proof that astrology must be true.
Correction: The author himself calls it a 'persuasive argument' (إقناعية), not a demonstrative one. Consensus does not guarantee truth but is presented as a strong rhetorical support.

Checkpoint
What is the second type of evidence used in the persuasive argument for astrology?
A) The sun's heat
B) The historical consensus of all people
C) The phases of the moon
D) The speed of planetary motion

Key Takeaway
The persuasive argument for astrology relies on observed correlations between celestial and terrestrial events and on the universal historical acceptance of astrology.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The author presents observed patterns (seasons, day/night) as a strong argument for astrology. In your own life, where might you be mistaking correlation for causation—especially regarding spiritual explanations for worldly events? How can you seek the real causes without falling into false induction?
?
Astrology claims celestial motions determine earthly events. Consider your own reliance on created causes: do you sometimes attribute outcomes to secondary causes in a way that diminishes your tawakkul in Allah? What specific habit can you change to trust Allah more directly?

Unseen Planets and Astrological Variations
Arguing for unseen planets causing variations in astrological influences and failures.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational argument positing unseen planets to explain why a planet's influence varies across zodiac signs and why astrological predictions often fail.

Core Idea
Astrology's failures point to hidden celestial variables.

This passage presents a philosophical argument that attempts to rescue astrology from contradiction. By observing that a planet's influence should be uniform across zodiac signs, but astrology reveals differences, the author posits the existence of small, unseen planets that modify each sign's nature. This reasoning not only explains astrological variations but also accounts for frequent failures in astrological predictions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the logical structure: principle, two options, conclusion.
2
Identify the logical principle and the two options
The passage starts with a principle: like things have like effects. Then it presents two explanations for the observed variation in astrological influences. Identify each option and see why one is rejected.
The rejected option is that signs have different natures; the accepted one is unseen planets.
3
Consider the sixth face about failures
The passage concludes with a sixth point: astrological indications often fail because of unknown planets. Think about how this supports the overall argument.
This connects the theoretical explanation to practical failure.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حال كونه في برج ، يجب أن يكون مساوياً لتأثيره حال كونه في سائر البروج ، لما ثبت في العقول أن حكم الشيء حكم مثله . ومعلوم أن ذلك على خلاف علم النجوم ، فأما أن يقال : إن طبائع البروج مختلفة بحسب الماهيات ، فذلك قول مردود عند الفلاسفة . أو يقال : إنه حصل في كل برج كواكب صغيرة لا نراها ولا نشاهدها، ولأجل حصول تلك الكواكب في تلك البروج ، صارت طبائع البروج مختلفة في التأثرات . وذلك هو المطلوب . الوجه السادس : إن الدلائل النجومية قد تختل وتفسد في كثير من الأوقات ، وما ذاك إلا بسبب ما ذكرنا . أنه حصلت هناك كواكب لا تعرفها ولأجلها تختلف أحوال هذه الآثار [ والله أعلم (۱)]
When it is in a sign, its influence must be equal to its influence when it is in other signs, because it is established in intellects that the judgment of a thing is the judgment of its like. And it is known that this contradicts the science of astrology. So either it is said that the natures of the signs differ according to essences, then that statement is rejected by the philosophers. Or it is said that in every sign there are small planets that we do not see or observe, and because of the presence of those planets in those signs, the natures of the signs become different in effects. And that is the desired conclusion. The sixth face: Indeed, astrological indications often become skewed and corrupted in many times, and that is only because of what we mentioned: that there are planets there that we do not know, and because of them the states of these effects vary. [And God knows best (1)]
Source pages p. 156

Commentary
This passage presents a combined argument. It begins by establishing a principle: a planet's influence should be identical across all signs because like things have like effects. Since this contradicts observed astrology, two explanations are considered. The first, that signs have different natures, is rejected by philosophers. The second, that unseen small planets in each sign cause the differences, is accepted. Then the sixth face states that astrological indications often fail precisely because of these unknown planets. Thus, the passage provides a rational defense of astrological failure by positing hidden variables.

Correction: The passage does not defend astrology; it explains why astrological predictions fail by positing hidden planets as variables.

The Three Ranks of Bodies and Planetary Influence
First proof for the third principle: hierarchy of bodies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the philosophical hierarchy of celestial bodies and why fixed stars are considered to have the strongest influence.

Core Idea
Fixed stars are strongest because they occupy the highest, unaffected sphere.

This passage introduces the third principle explaining why knowing planetary natures is difficult. The first proof relies on a philosophical consensus that bodies are arranged in three ranks, from the unaffected highest sphere to the affected lower spheres. Understanding this hierarchy helps explain why fixed stars dominate.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Note that it presents a tripartite hierarchy of celestial bodies.
The passage is the beginning of the first of two proofs.
2
Identify the three ranks
List the three ranks: the unaffected (highest sphere and fixed stars), the affected that do not affect (lower spheres of air/fire and water/earth), and the middle rank (seven spheres of moving planets).
Rank 1 is 'does not receive effect', rank 2 is 'affected and affects', rank 3 is 'affected but does not affect'.
3
Connect to the main claim
Understand that the fixed stars, being in the highest rank, have the strongest influence, which is why their natures are more difficult to know (the passage is building toward that).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأصل الثالث من الأصول الموجبة لصعوبة هذا العلم : إن الوقوف على طبيعة كل كوكب بحسب تأثيره صعب عسير . وتقريره . أن نقول : لا شك أن الكواكب إما ثابتة وإما سيارة . أما الكواكب الثابتة فإن تأثيراتها أقوى من تأثيرات السيارة . ويدل عليه و جهان (۱) مراتب . الأول : إنا بينا أن الفلاسفة اتفقوا على أن الأجسام مرتبة على ثلاث مراتب . المرتبة الأولى : الذي لا يتأثر . وهما الكرتان العاليتان . أعني الفلك الأعظم ، وفلك الثوابت . وهذه المرتبة أشرف المراتب وأعلاها . والمرتبة الأخيرة : هي مرتبة الجسم، الذي يتأثر ولا يؤثر وهما الكرتان السافلتان إحداهما : كرة اللطيف، أعني الهواء والنار . والثانية : كرة الكثيف أعني الماء والأرض . فهاتان الكرتان : يقبلان الأثر من الكرات العالية ، وليس لها تأثير في شيء آخر . وأما المرتبة المتوسطة . فهي التي تقبل الآثار من السيارات عن الكرتين العاليتين ، وتؤديانه إلى الكرتين السافلتين ، وهو الكرات السبعة التي حصل فيها السيارات السبعة. وهذا الرأي متفق عليه بين الفلاسفة . والاستقصاء فيه مذكور في باب صفات الكواكب . وهذا الاعتبار يدل
The third principle of the principles that necessitate the difficulty of this science: Knowing the nature of each planet according to its influence is difficult and hard. Its explanation: We say: There is no doubt that planets are either fixed or moving. As for the fixed planets, their influences are stronger than the influences of the moving ones. This is indicated by two aspects, (1) ranks. The first: We have shown that the philosophers agreed that bodies are arranged in three ranks. The first rank: that which is not affected: the two upper spheres, i.e., the highest celestial sphere and the sphere of the fixed stars. This rank is the most honorable and highest. The last rank: the rank of the body that is affected but does not affect: the two lower spheres, one of them the sphere of the subtle, i.e., air and fire, and the second the sphere of the dense, i.e., water and earth. These two spheres receive effect from the higher spheres and have no effect on anything else. The middle rank: that which receives effects from the moving [planets] from the two upper spheres and transmits them to the two lower spheres, which are the seven spheres in which the seven moving planets are found. This opinion is agreed upon among the philosophers. The exhaustive treatment of this is mentioned in the chapter on the attributes of the planets. And this consideration indicates
Source pages p. 157

Commentary
This passage starts the third principle, which is the difficulty of knowing each planet's nature and influence. It explains that planets are either fixed or moving, and fixed ones have stronger influence. This is supported by two aspects, but only the first is given: the philosophical consensus that bodies are arranged in three ranks. The first rank (unaffected) comprises the highest sphere and the fixed stars, which are most honorable. The last rank (affected, non-affecting) comprises the spheres of air/fire and water/earth. The middle rank (affecting and being affected) comprises the seven spheres of the moving planets. This hierarchy implies that fixed planets, being in the first rank, have the strongest influence. The passage notes that further detail is in the chapter on planetary attributes and that this consideration leads to a conclusion that is not included.

Correction: The passage attributes their strength to their rank in the philosophical hierarchy: they belong to the highest sphere, which is unaffected and therefore the most influential.

The Third Principle: Difficulty of Knowing Planetary Natures
Al-Razi states the third principle and argues via three-rank hierarchy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the third principle that makes astrology difficult and the three-rank hierarchy of bodies used to prove the superiority of fixed stars.

Core Idea
Fixed stars are superior because they occupy the highest rank in the cosmic hierarchy.

Al-Razi introduces the third obstacle to accurate astrology: the impossibility of fully knowing each planet's nature. He then begins to demonstrate the greater influence of fixed stars over planets by recalling the philosophical consensus on a three-tiered universe. This lesson walks you through that hierarchy and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Understand the third principle
Read the opening and note why Al-Razi says it is difficult to know the nature of each planet according to its influence.
This sets up the problem that astrology faces.
2
Learn the three ranks
Identify the three ranks: (1) highest spheres that do not receive influence, (2) middle spheres that receive and transmit, (3) lowest spheres that only receive.
The highest rank includes the Supreme Sphere and the Sphere of Fixed Stars.
3
Understand the conclusion
Realize that this hierarchy implies that fixed stars are stronger and more complete than the wandering planets.
The hierarchy is agreed upon by philosophers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأصل الثالث من الأصول الموجبة لصعوبة هذا العلم : إن الوقوف على طبيعة كل كوكب بحسب تأثيره صعب عسير . وتقريره . أن نقول : لا شك أن الكواكب إما ثابتة وإما سيارة . أما الكواكب الثابتة فإن تأثيراتها أقوى من تأثيرات السيارة . ويدل عليه وجهان [؟] : الأول : إنا بينا أن الفلاسفة اتفقوا على أن الأجسام مرتبة على ثلاث مراتب . المرتبة الأولى : الذي لا يتأثر . وهما الكرتان العاليتان . أعني الفلك الأعظم ، وفلك الثوابت . وهذه المرتبة أشرف المراتب وأعلاها . والمرتبة الأخيرة : هي مرتبة الجسم، الذي يتأثر ولا يؤثر وهما الكرتان السافلتان إحداهما : كرة اللطيف، أعني الهواء والنار . والثانية : كرة الكثيف أعني الماء والأرض . فهاتان الكرتان : يقبلان الأثر من الكرات العالية ، وليس لها تأثير في شيء آخر . وأما المرتبة المتوسطة . فهي التي تقبل الآثار من السيارات عن الكرتين العاليتين ، وتؤديانه إلى الكرتين السافلتين ، وهو الكرات السبعة التي حصل فيها السيارات السبعة. وهذا الرأي متفق عليه بين الفلاسفة . والاستقصاء فيه مذكور في باب صفات الكواكب . وهذا الاعتبار يدل على سبيل الإجمال : أن الثوابت أقوى وأكمل من السيارات . والوجه الثالث في بيان أن الثوابت أقوى من السيارات : هو أنها أكمل من السيارات في أمور ثلاثة : أولها : أنها أقرب في درجة المعلولية ، والعبودية إلى المبدأ الأول من هذه السيارات ، وذلك القرب هو المنبع لكل الكمالات . وثانيها : أنها كثيرة في العدد جداً ، والكثرة مظنة القوة ، وأيضاً : فالثوابت التي في العظم الأول [أكبر] قدراً من كل السيارات إلا الشمس . والعظم في الجرمية ، يفيد العظم في القوة . وثالثها : أنها أبطأ حركة . فيكون بقاؤها في الدرجة الواحدة أدوم . وقد علمت في الطبيعيات : أن دوام المسامتة ، يوجب كمال القوة . فثبت بهذه البيانات : أن الكواكب الثابتة أقوى قوة ، وأكمل تأثيراً من السيارات
The third principle among the principles necessitating the difficulty of this science: that comprehending the nature of every planet according to its influence is difficult and arduous. And its exposition: we say: there is no doubt that the planets are either fixed or wandering. As for the fixed stars, their influences are stronger than the influences of the wanderers (planets). And this is indicated by two aspects [؟]: First: we have shown that the philosophers agreed that bodies are arranged in three ranks. The first rank: that which does not receive influence. They are the two highest spheres, namely the Supreme Sphere and the Sphere of the Fixed Stars. And this rank is the most noble and highest of ranks. The last rank: it is the rank of the body that receives influence but does not exert influence, and they are the two lower spheres: one of them the sphere of the subtle, namely air and fire; the second: the sphere of the dense, namely water and earth. These two spheres receive influence from the high spheres, and they have no influence on anything else. As for the middle rank: it is that which receives influences from the wanderers (planets) from the two high spheres, and conveys them to the two lower spheres, and it is the seven spheres in which the seven wanderers (planets) are found. This opinion is agreed upon among the philosophers. Detailed discussion of it is mentioned in the chapter on the attributes of the planets. And this consideration indicates in summary: that the fixed stars are stronger and more complete than the wanderers. And the third aspect in explaining that the fixed stars are stronger than the wanderers: is that they are more complete than the wanderers in three matters: First: they are closer in the degree of effecthood and servitude to the First Principle (al-mabda' al-awwal) than these wanderers, and that closeness is the source of all perfections. Second: they are very numerous in number, and multitude is a locus of strength, and also: the fixed stars that are in the first magnitude are greater in measure than every wanderer except the sun. And greatness in corporeality yields greatness in strength. Third: they are slower in motion, so their abiding in one degree is more lasting. And you have learned in the natural sciences that continuity of alignment necessitates perfection of strength. So it is established by these evidences that the fixed stars are stronger in power and more complete in influence than the wanderers.
Source pages p. 157

Commentary
This passage presents the third principle that makes astrology difficult: the impossibility of thoroughly knowing the nature of each planet's influence. Al-Razi then proves that fixed stars are stronger than planets. He argues that there is no doubt that stars are either fixed or wandering, and fixed stars have stronger effects. He gives two lines of proof: First, he recalls that philosophers agree on three ranks of bodies: (1) the highest spheres (the Supreme Sphere and Sphere of Fixed Stars) that do not receive influence; (2) the lowest spheres (air/fire and water/earth) that only receive influence; and (3) the middle spheres (the seven planetary spheres) that both receive from above and convey to below. This hierarchy shows that fixed stars are stronger and more complete. Second, he presents a third aspect (having previously mentioned two? the text is unclear) that fixed stars are superior in three ways: (a) closer to the First Principle (God) in effecthood and servitude, (b) more numerous and larger (except the sun), and (c) slower in motion, making their alignment more lasting and thus stronger. He concludes that these proofs establish the greater power and influence of fixed stars.

Key Terms
الكواكب الثابتة
السيارات
المراتب الثلاث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that all celestial bodies have equal influence or that the lowest spheres are active.
Correction: The passage shows a strict hierarchy: highest spheres are purely active, middle spheres are passive-active, and lowest spheres are purely passive. Fixed stars belong to the highest rank, making them superior.

Checkpoint

D) The spheres of water and earth

Key Takeaway
The fixed stars belong to the highest rank that does not receive influence, making them stronger and more complete than planets.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Razi presents a hierarchy where the highest bodies only give and never receive. What would it take for you to strive toward that higher rank of self-sufficiency in your faith?

?
If the fixed stars are 'stronger and more complete' because they belong to the highest rank, what does that say about your own spiritual aspirations? Are you actively seeking to be in a position of strength through direct connection with the Divine, or are you content to be in the middle, merely transmitting what others teach you?

Proof of Fixed Stars' Superiority: Three Aspects
Al-Razi enumerates three aspects proving fixed stars' superiority.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three specific reasons why fixed stars are more powerful than planets according to Al-Razi.

Core Idea
Fixed stars are closer to God, more numerous, larger, and slower-moving, all contributing to their greater influence.

After establishing the general hierarchy, Al-Razi provides three concrete arguments demonstrating the superiority of fixed stars over planets. These arguments combine metaphysical closeness, quantitative strength, and physical properties of motion and alignment. This lesson examines each argument and its basis.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the full passage to see the three matters in which fixed stars are more complete.
These are explicitly enumerated as first, second, and third.
2
First argument: closeness to the First Principle
Notice that fixed stars are closer to the First Principle in terms of effecthood and servitude, which is the source of all perfections.
This is a metaphysical reason.
3
Second argument: number and size
Fixed stars are very numerous and large (except the sun); both number and size indicate strength.
Quantitative superiority matters in astrology.
4
Third argument: slower motion
Fixed stars move slower, so they remain in one degree longer. Longer alignment means stronger influence.
Physical continuity enhances effect.

The third principle among the principles necessitating the difficulty of this science: that comprehending the nature of every planet according to its influence is difficult and arduous. And its exposition: we say: there is no doubt that the planets are either fixed or wandering. As for the fixed stars, their influences are stronger than the influences of the wanderers (planets). And this is indicated by two aspects [؟]: First: we have shown that the philosophers agreed that bodies are arranged in three ranks. The first rank: that which does not receive influence. They are the two highest spheres, namely the Supreme Sphere and the Sphere of the Fixed Stars. And this rank is the most noble and highest of ranks. The last rank: it is the rank of the body that receives influence but does not exert influence, and they are the two lower spheres: one of them the sphere of the subtle, namely air and fire; the second: the sphere of the dense, namely water and earth. These two spheres receive influence from the high spheres, and they have no influence on anything else. As for the middle rank: it is that which receives influences from the wanderers (planets) from the two high spheres, and conveys them to the two lower spheres, and it is the seven spheres in which the seven wanderers (planets) are found. This opinion is agreed upon among the philosophers. Detailed discussion of it is mentioned in the chapter on the attributes of the planets. And this consideration indicates in summary: that the fixed stars are stronger and more complete than the wanderers. And the third aspect in explaining that the fixed stars are stronger than the wanderers: is that they are more complete than the wanderers in three matters: First: they are closer in the degree of effecthood and servitude to the First Principle (al-mabda' al-awwal) than these wanderers, and that closeness is the source of all perfections. Second: they are very numerous in number, and multitude is a locus of strength, and also: the fixed stars that are in the first magnitude are greater in measure than every wanderer except the sun. And greatness in corporeality yields greatness in strength. Third: they are slower in motion, so their abiding in one degree is more lasting. And you have learned in the natural sciences that continuity of alignment necessitates perfection of strength. So it is established by these evidences that the fixed stars are stronger in power and more complete in influence than the wanderers.
Source pages p. 157

Commentary
This passage presents the third principle that makes astrology difficult: the impossibility of thoroughly knowing the nature of each planet's influence. Al-Razi then proves that fixed stars are stronger than planets. He argues that there is no doubt that stars are either fixed or wandering, and fixed stars have stronger effects. He gives two lines of proof: First, he recalls that philosophers agree on three ranks of bodies: (1) the highest spheres (the Supreme Sphere and Sphere of Fixed Stars) that do not receive influence; (2) the lowest spheres (air/fire and water/earth) that only receive influence; and (3) the middle spheres (the seven planetary spheres) that both receive from above and convey to below. This hierarchy shows that fixed stars are stronger and more complete. Second, he presents a third aspect (having previously mentioned two? the text is unclear) that fixed stars are superior in three ways: (a) closer to the First Principle (God) in effecthood and servitude, (b) more numerous and larger (except the sun), and (c) slower in motion, making their alignment more lasting and thus stronger. He concludes that these proofs establish the greater power and influence of fixed stars.

Misconception: One might think that faster motion indicates stronger influence.
Correction: Al-Razi argues that slower motion leads to longer alignment and thus stronger effect.

Key Takeaway
