Al-Razi's Epistemic Critique of Astrology: Fixed Stars and Planetary Combinations
Al-Razi enumerates two insurmountable difficulties in astrology: ignorance of fixed stars and infinite planetary complexity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Al-Razi's two-part argument that astrology suffers from insurmountable ignorance and infinite complexity, making it epistemically unsound.

Core Idea
Astrology fails because astrologers admit ignorance and infinite factors make knowledge impossible.

Al-Razi continues his critique of astrology by exposing two fundamental epistemic obstacles. First, astrologers themselves confess to knowing almost nothing about fixed stars. Second, even if planetary natures were known, the infinite combinations of positions and overriding ascendants make certain prediction impossible. This passage shows that astrology's problems are not just practical but logical and infinite.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Let Al-Razi's argument unfold naturally.
The passage ends mid-sentence due to a page break, but the main points are clear.
2
Identify the two broad arguments
The passage first discusses ignorance about fixed stars, then turns to difficulties with planets even if their natures were known. Identify these two main sections.
3
Examine the planetary sub-difficulties
Within the planetary section, Al-Razi lists two specific difficulties: infinite combinations and the overriding effect of original ascendants. Note each one.
The word 'وبحسب الأحوال' hints at additional unspecified conditions.
4
Reflect on the infinite complexity argument
Why does Al-Razi consider infinite combinations a decisive problem? Consider the principle that what is infinite cannot be fully known by finite minds.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأيضاً : الأحكاميون اتفقوا على أنه إذا وقع منها على موضع معين من الطوالع أعطت عطايا قوية إما في السعادة ، أو في النحوسة . وإذا ثبت هذا فنقول: إن الأحكاميين اتفقوا على أنهم لم يعرفوا من طبائعها إلا القليل . وإذا كان الأمر كذلك ، فقد ظهر الخبط والصعوبة في هذا العلم ، بسبب الجهل . وأما السيارات : فنقول : هب أن طبائعها صارت معلومة ، إلا أنه بقيت الصعوبة من وجوه : الأول : إن إمتزاجات الكواكب ، ومناسباتها بحسب كل : حد ، ووجه ، ومثله ومنزل من منازل القمر ، ودرجة معينة من الدرجات الثلثمائة وستين . تصير غير متناهية ، وما لا ينتهي لا يمكن معرفته ؟ والثاني : هب أن مواضع الكواكب وامتزاجاتها صارت معلومة ، إلا أن احكام طوالع الوقت قد تندفع بحسب الطوالع الأصلية ، وبحسب الأحوال
And also: the astrologers (ahkamiyyun) agreed that when [a fixed star] falls upon a specific place among the ascendants, it gives strong gifts, either in fortune or misfortune. And when this is established, we say: the astrologers agreed that they know only a little of their natures. And if the matter is so, then confusion and difficulty in this science have become apparent, due to ignorance. As for the wanderers (planets), we say: suppose their natures became known, except that difficulty remains in aspects: First: the mixtures of the planets and their correlations according to each term (hadd), face (wajh), and like it, and a lunar station (manzil), and a specific degree among the three hundred and sixty degrees become infinite, and that which does not end cannot be known. Second: suppose that the positions of the planets and their mixtures became known, except that the judgments of the time ascendants may be repelled according to the original ascendants and according to the conditions.
Source pages p. 158

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of difficulties in astrology. Al-Razi first addresses fixed stars: astrologers agree that fixed stars give powerful influences when they align with specific ascendants, yet they also admit that they know only a little of their natures. This ignorance causes confusion and difficulty. Then he turns to the planets (wanderers). Even if their individual natures were fully known, two difficulties remain: First, the combinations and correlations of planets with each other, considering positions like terms, faces, lunar stations, and specific degrees among 360, are infinite, and what is infinite cannot be fully known. Second, even if positions and mixtures were known, the judgments of the time ascendants (horoscopes) can be repelled or overridden by the original ascendants and by conditions (presumably other astrological factors), making precise prediction impossible. The passage ends abruptly, but the point is clear: astrology suffers from insurmountable epistemic obstacles.

The Receptive Cause and the Value of Astrology
The author presents the third point about the receptive cause and concludes on astrology's difficulty and benefit.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the receptive cause makes astrological predictions incomplete yet still valuable, and why scholars deemed the pursuit of astrology obligatory.

Core Idea
The same celestial cause yields different effects due to variable matter, yet partial knowledge is still beneficial.

Having discussed earlier obstacles to perfect astrological knowledge, the author now presents a third: the receptive cause. Even if celestial influences are constant, earthly matter receiving them is highly variable, making exact prediction impossible. Yet this does not render the science useless; instead, reason and experience show its immense practical benefit.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation. Let the author's argument unfold.
Notice how the third point builds on the earlier ones.
2
Identify the two causes
Find where the author mentions the efficient cause and the receptive cause. Understand their roles in producing an effect.
The efficient cause is the celestial influence; the receptive cause is the earthly matter.
3
Study the example
The author gives an example of a king's son and a baker's son born under the same ascendant. Consider why the effects differ.
This illustrates the variability of sublunar matter.
4
Grasp the conclusion
The author concludes that full knowledge is difficult but the science should not be abandoned. Induction shows great benefit, so it is obligatory to study it.
The principle: 'what cannot be fully grasped should not be entirely abandoned' is key.
5
Reflect on the obligation
Ask yourself why the author says 'it is obligatory to occupy oneself with acquiring it.' What does this say about the value of partial knowledge?
This lesson challenges the idea that imperfect knowledge is useless.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الماضية في الفلك. ومن الذي يمكنه الوقوف على جميع الأحوال الماضية في الفلك ؟ والثالث : إنه كما يعتبر في حصول الأثر ، حصول العلة الفاعلية فكذلك يعتبر في حصوله العلة القابلية ، ولهذا السبب اتفق المنجمون على أنه إذا ولد على الطالع الواحد : ابن مالك ، وابن قصاب . أو خباز فإنه لا يتساوى أثر ذلك الطالع فيهم . فعلمنا : أن آثار الطوالع تختلف بحسب اختلاف أحوال المادة السفلية ، لكن المواد السفلية سريعة التغير ، شديدة التبدل فكيف يمكن الوقوف على أحوالها ؟ فهذا ضبط الوجوه المذكورة في بيان أن الوقوف على أحوال هذا العالم بالتمام . والكمال صعب ، إلا أن العقلاء اتفقوا على أن ما لا يدرك كله ، لا يترك كله ، فهذا العلم وإن كان صعب المرام من هذه الوجوه ، إلا أن الاستقراء يدل على حصول النفع العظيم منه . وإذا كان كذلك ، وجب الاشتغال بتحصيله ، والاعتناء بشأنه، فإن القليل منه كثير ، بالنسبة إلى أحوال مصالح البشر والله أعلم.
The past [states] in the celestial sphere. And who can fully know all the past states in the celestial sphere? And the third: just as the occurrence of the efficient cause is considered [necessary] for the production of the effect, so too the occurrence of the receptive cause is considered [necessary] for its production. For this reason the astrologers agreed that if a king's son and a butcher's son or a baker [are born] under the same ascendant, the effect of that ascendant is not equal in them. So we know that the effects of the ascendants differ according to the differing states of the sublunar matter. But sublunar matters are swift to change, extremely variable. So how can one fully know their states? So this is a summary of the mentioned aspects [showing] that full and perfect knowledge of the states of this world is difficult. However, the rational people agreed that what cannot be fully grasped should not be entirely abandoned. So this science, although difficult to attain from these aspects, induction indicates that immense benefit is obtained from it. If so, then it is obligatory to occupy oneself with acquiring it and to care for its matter, for a little of it is much in relation to the affairs of human welfare. And God knows best.
Source pages p. 159

Commentary
This passage presents the third argument for the difficulty of fully knowing astrological influences, followed by a conclusion that despite this difficulty, the science is beneficial and should be pursued. The author begins by referencing earlier points (the first two are not given here) and then states the third: just as the efficient cause (al-illa al-fa'iliyya) is necessary for an effect, so too is the receptive cause (al-illa al-qabiliyya). The receptive cause here refers to the disposition of the sublunar matter (al-madda al-sufliyya) receiving the celestial influence. Astrologers acknowledge that the same ascendant can produce different effects in different individuals (e.g., a king's son vs. a baker's son) due to differences in their material constitution. This shows that sublunar matter is highly variable and changing, making it impossible to fully know its states. The author then summarizes all the mentioned points (al-wujuh al-madhkura) concluding that complete knowledge of this world's states is difficult. However, reason dictates that what cannot be fully known should not be entirely abandoned. Induction (al-istiqra') shows that great benefit is derived from this science. Therefore, one must engage in studying it, as even a little is much for human welfare. The phrase 'And God knows best' ends the discussion.

Celestial Causes: Proofs for Fixed Stars' Superiority
Classifies celestial causes and presents three proofs for fixed stars' strength.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three proofs given for the fixed stars being stronger than planets in celestial causation.

Core Idea
Fixed stars are stronger because they are closer to the First Principle, larger, and slower-moving.

This passage begins the detailed discussion of celestial effective causes. After classifying celestial causes into three types, the author focuses on planets and divides them into wandering and fixed. He then presents three compelling proofs for why fixed stars are stronger in effect than planets, drawing on proximity to the First Principle, size, and motion. The passage ends with the start of an objection that will be answered later.

Guided Path
1
Read the classification and division
Note the three types of celestial causes: planets, points, constellations. Then focus on planets divided into wandering and fixed.
The term 'wandering' refers to the planets proper, while 'fixed' are the stars.
2
Identify the claim and three proofs
The claim is that fixed stars are stronger. Read each proof carefully: proximity to First Principle, size (except Sun), and slower motion leading to more permanent pores.
The proofs rely on Aristotelian physics concepts like 'pores' (مسامات) which are thought to be channels for celestial influence.
3
Consider the incomplete objection
The passage starts an objection arguing that planets should be stronger, but it cuts off. Think about what counterarguments might be.
This leads into the next lesson.

Source Text

القسم الأول من الفصل الخامس في تفصيل أحوال المؤثرات العلوية أعلم : أن الأسباب السماوية : إما الكواكب . وإما النقط . وإما البروج . النوع الأول البحث عن أنواع الكواكب واعلم : أنها إما سيارة ، وإما ثابتة . أما السيارات : فقد أطبقوا على أنها مؤثرات في أحوال هذا العالم . وأما الثوابت ، فلقائل أن يقول : إنها أقوى في التأثير من السيارات . ويدل عليه وجوه : الأول : إنها أقرب في درجة المعلولية من المبدأ الأول . وذلك يوجب كمال القوة . والثاني : إن التي في العظم الأول منها : أعظم جرماً من السيارة . إلا الشمس . والثالث : إنها أبطأ حركة فتكون مساماتها أدوم ، فتكون أقوى في التأثير . ولقائل أن يقول إنه يجب أن تكون السيارات أقوى في
First Section of Chapter Five: On Details of the Celestial Effective Causes. Know that the celestial causes are either the planets, or the points, or the constellations. The first type: investigation of the kinds of planets. Know: they are either wandering or fixed. As for the wandering ones, they have agreed that they are effective in the states of this world. As for the fixed ones, one may say that they are stronger in effect than the wandering ones. And evidence for it has aspects: First: they are closer in degree of effecthood to the First Principle, and that necessitates perfection of power. Second: those in the first greatness among them are larger in body than the wandering ones, except the sun. Third: they are slower in motion, so their pores are more permanent, so they are stronger in effect. And one may say that it is necessary that the wandering ones be stronger in ...
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage begins the detailed discussion of celestial effective causes. The author first states that celestial causes are of three types: planets, points, and constellations. He then focuses on the first type, planets, which are divided into wandering (planets) and fixed stars. He notes that there is agreement that wandering planets affect worldly affairs, but then presents the possibility that fixed stars are stronger. Three proofs are given: First, fixed stars are closer in rank of being caused to the First Principle, which implies greater power. Second, the largest fixed stars are greater in size than the planets, except the sun. Third, fixed stars move more slowly, so their 'pores' remain longer, making their effect stronger. The passage then begins an objection arguing that planets should be stronger, but this objection is cut off at the page break, so the answer is not included here.

Celestial Causes: Planets, Nodes, and Signs
Author classifies celestial causes and argues for planetary influence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author classifies celestial causes and the arguments for the influence of planets versus fixed stars.

Core Idea
The debate on planetary influence turns on proximity, motion, and causal suitability.

In this passage, the author begins by classifying the heavenly causes into planets, nodal points, and zodiac signs. He then distinguishes between wandering planets and fixed stars, and presents two opposing views on their influence. This lesson will guide you through the classification and the key arguments.

Guided Path
1
Read the classification
Notice the threefold division: planets (kawakib), nodal points (nuqat), and zodiac signs (buruj). Then focus on the subcategory of planets: wandering (sayyara) and fixed (thabita).
The classification sets the stage for the debate.
2
Examine arguments for fixed stars
Read the three proofs claiming fixed stars are stronger: (1) closer to the First Principle, (2) larger size, (3) slower motion. Understand each reasoning.
These are based on Aristotelian causal chains.
3
Examine arguments for wandering planets
Read the four counter-proofs: (1) proximity to our world, (2) fixed stars cannot cause change, (3) planets change relative positions, (4) planets mix lights. Note the conclusion.
The author sides with the planets as more important.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القسم الأول من الفصل الخامس في تفصيل أحوال المؤثرات العلوية (۱) : أن الأسباب السماوية : إما الكواكب . وإما النقط (٢) وإما البروج (۳). النوع الأول البحث عن أنواع الكواكب واعلم : أنها إما سيارة ، وإما ثابتة . أما السيارات : فقد أطبقوا على أنها مؤثرات في أحوال هذا العالم . وأما الثوابت ، فلقائل أن يقول : إنها أقوى في التأثير من السيارات . ويدل عليه وجوه : الأول : إنها أقرب في درجة المعلولية (٥) من المبدأ الأول . وذلك يوجب كمال القوة . والثاني : إن التي في العظم الأول منها : أعظم جرماً من السيارة . إلا الشمس (٦) . والثالث : إنها أبطأ حركة فتكون مساماتها أدوم ، فتكون أقوى في التأثير . ولقائل (۷) أن يقول إنه يجب أن تكون (۸) السيارات أقوى في التأثير (۱) ويدل عليه وجوه : الأول : إنها أقرب إلى هذا العالم من تلك الثوابت . والثاني : إن الثوابت كاسمها ثوابت. فلا يليق بها أن تكون عللا لهذه الحوادث ، التي هي سريعة التغير في هذا العالم . والثالث : إن الثوابت لا يتغير نسب بعضها إلى بعض ، لا في الطول ولا في العرض. لأنها مركوزة في كرة واحدة ، بخلاف السيارات ، فإن كل واحدة منها مركوزة في كرة اخرى ولكل كرة حركة على حدة فلا حركات كراتها في الأطوال وفي العروض . فتحصل النسب المختلفة التي يمكن ان تكون مبادىء الحدوث الحوادث في هذا العالم . والرابع : إن هذه السيارات تمر بتلك الثوابت ، فتمتزج بهذا الطريق أنوار بعض تلك الثوابت بالبعض . فثبت بهذا الطريق أن الأهم في عالم النجوم معرفة طبائع السيارات ثم بعدها معرفة طبائع الثوابت.
The first section of the fifth chapter on detailing the states of the celestial influences: (1) The heavenly causes are either the planets, or the nodal points, or the zodiac signs. The first type: investigation of the types of planets. Know: they are either wandering or fixed. As for the wandering planets, they have agreed that they are influences on the states of this world. As for the fixed stars, someone may say: they are stronger in influence than the wandering planets. And it is indicated by aspects: First: they are closer in the degree of effect (ma'luliyya) to the First Principle. And that necessitates perfection of power. Second: those among them that are in the first magnitude are greater in body than the wandering planets, except the sun. Third: they are slower in motion so their pores are more enduring, so they are stronger in influence. And someone may say that the wandering planets must be stronger in influence, and it is indicated by aspects: First: they are closer to this world than those fixed stars. Second: the fixed stars, as their name indicates, are fixed. So it is not fitting for them to be causes for these events which are rapidly changing in this world. Third: the fixed stars do not change their relations to each other, neither in longitude nor latitude, because they are fixed in one sphere, unlike the wandering planets, for each of them is fixed in another sphere and each sphere has its own motion, so their spheres' motions vary in longitudes and latitudes. Thus different relations are obtained which can be principles for the occurrence of events in this world. Fourth: these wandering planets pass by those fixed stars, and by this way the lights of some of those fixed stars mix with others. So it is established by this way that the most important in the world of stars is knowledge of the natures of the wandering planets, then after it knowledge of the natures of the fixed stars.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage classifies celestial causes and presents a dialectical argument. The author begins by dividing celestial causes into three types: planets (كواكب), nodal points (النقط), and zodiac signs (البروج). He then specifies that planets are either wandering (سيارة) or fixed (ثابتة). He notes that scholars agree wandering planets affect this world, but some argue fixed stars are stronger. Three proofs are given for fixed stars: (1) they are closer to the First Principle in the chain of causality, (2) larger in size except the sun, (3) slower motion leading to longer duration of effect. Then a counter-argument is presented with four proofs for wandering planets: (1) closer to this world, (2) fixed stars are unchanging and thus unsuitable to cause change, (3) wandering planets change relative positions and thus produce different relations that can be principles of change, (4) wandering planets pass by fixed stars and mix their lights. The conclusion is that the most important knowledge in the stellar world is the natures of wandering planets, then fixed stars.

كواكب سيارة
كواكب ثابتة
بروج
نقط
معلولية
مبدأ أول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The author denies any influence from fixed stars.
Correction: The author says fixed stars have influence but wandering planets are more important because they are closer and produce variable relations.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the most important knowledge in the stellar world?
A) Natures of fixed stars
B) Natures of wandering planets
C) Natures of the moon
D) Natures of the zodiac signs

Key Takeaway
The most important knowledge in the stellar world is the natures of wandering planets, followed by fixed stars.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The author concludes that wandering planets are more important because they interact and produce diverse relations. Are you attentive to how God uses changing conditions to guide and test you? Or do you dismiss the 'wandering' as mere chance?
?
One argument says fixed stars are closer to the First Principle. Reflect: Are you more drawn to the immediate, visible influences (people, events) or to the unseen ultimate Cause? What concrete step can you take today to turn your heart more toward God as the First Principle?

The Moon's Special Importance in Celestial Influence
Author justifies the moon's primacy via two reasons.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the moon is considered the most important celestial body to study according to the author.

Core Idea
The moon is the key intermediary for celestial influence on Earth.

The author continues his hierarchy of importance among celestial bodies, now focusing on the moon. He presents four reasons for its preeminence, though only the first two survive in this passage. These reasons center on the moon's unique role as a direct intermediary between the higher planets and our changing world.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once through, then the translation. Notice the logical structure: the author first makes an analogy, then introduces the four reasons, and elaborates the first two.
The passage breaks off after the second reason due to a page break.
2
Identify the two given reasons
Find the first and second reasons. Understand the claim that the moon's effects reach directly without an intermediary, while other planets' effects come through the moon.
The phrase 'من غير واسطة' (without intermediary) is key.
3
Reflect on the cosmological model
Consider the geocentric model where the moon is the closest celestial body. Think about why proximity and direct influence would make its study more important.
4
Connect to the common misunderstanding
The text emphasizes that the moon is an intermediary, not a primary cause. This corrects the notion that the moon itself causes changes independently.
The common misunderstanding is addressed in the misconception section.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أنه كما أن البحث عن طبائع السيارات أهم من البحث عن طبائع الثوابت فكذا البحث عن معرفة أحوال القمر أهم المهمات . لأن الأسباب الأربعة المذكورة موجودة فيه : فالأول : إن أقرب الكواكب إلى هذا العالم : القمر . وآثاره تصل إلى هذا العالم من غير واسطة . وإما آثار سائر الكواكب فإنها لا تصل إلى هذا العالم إلا بواسطة القمر . فوجب أن يكون البحث عن حال القمر ، أهم من غيره . والثاني : إن أحوال هذا العالم سريعة التغير والدوران . وأحوال القمر أيضاً كذلك .
And know that just as the investigation into the natures of the wandering planets is more important than the investigation into the natures of the fixed stars, so too the investigation into the knowledge of the states of the moon is the most important of important matters. Because the four mentioned reasons are present in it: The first: The closest of the planets to this world is the moon. And its effects reach this world without an intermediary. As for the effects of the rest of the planets, they do not reach this world except through the moon. So necessarily the investigation into the state of the moon is more important than other matters. The second: The states of this world are rapidly changing and revolving. And the states of the moon are also likewise.
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage continues the theme of importance, focusing on the moon. The author states that just as studying planets is more important than fixed stars, studying the moon is even more important. He gives four reasons (only the first two are fully preserved in the text): First, the moon is the closest planet to this world and its effects reach directly without an intermediary, while other planets affect only through the moon. Second, the states of this world are rapidly changing, and the moon's states are similarly rapid. The text breaks off before the third and fourth reasons, but this suffices to show the moon's special status.

Why Planets Surpass Fixed Stars in Causal Importance
The author enumerates four reasons why planets are more important than fixed stars.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four rational arguments that establish the planets' causal significance over the fixed stars in generating earthly events.

Core Idea
Planets, not fixed stars, drive change because they are close, mutable, and mix their lights.

Before discussing the moon's special role, the author first establishes a general principle: that planets (al-sayyārāt) are more causally relevant to earthly events than fixed stars. He presents four clear arguments, each grounded in observation and reasoning. This lesson walks through those four arguments and why they shift the focus of study from the fixed stars to the planets.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the four reasons
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Try to locate the four distinct reasons given for the planets' superiority.
The reasons are introduced with 'الأول', 'والثاني', etc.
2
Understand the first reason: proximity
The first reason is that planets are closer to our world than fixed stars. Consider why proximity matters for causal influence.
3
Understand the second reason: suitability from changeability
Fixed stars are fixed, while earthly events are rapidly changing. The author argues that only changing entities can be causes of changing effects.
This is a logical argument: like causes like.
4
Understand the third and fourth reasons: variability and light mixing
The third reason is that planets move relative to each other, creating diverse relationships that can cause various events. The fourth is that planets mix the lights of fixed stars as they pass by.
These reasons emphasize the dynamic nature of planets.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
التأثير ويدل عليه وجوه:
الأول: إنها أقرب إلى هذا العالم من تلك الثوابت.
والثاني: إن الثوابت كاسمها ثوابت. فلا يليق بها أن تكون عللا لهذه الحوادث التي هي سريعة التغير في هذا العالم.
والثالث: إن الثوابت لا يتغير نسب بعضها إلى بعض، لا في الطول ولا في العرض. لأنها مركوزة في كرة واحدة، بخلاف السيارات، فإن كل واحدة منها مركوزة في كرة أخرى ولكل كرة حركة على حدة. فلا حركات كراتها في الأطوال وفي العروض. فتحصل النسب المختلفة التي يمكن أن تكون مبادىء حدوث الحوادث في هذا العالم.
والرابع: إن هذه السيارات تمر بتلك الثوابت، فتمتزج بهذا الطريق أنوار بعض تلك الثوابت بالبعض.
فثبت بهذا الطريق: أن الأهم في عالم النجوم: معرفة طبائع السيارات ثم بعدها معرفة طبائع الثوابت. واعلم أنه كما أن البحث عن طبائع السيارات أهم من البحث عن طبائع الثوابت، فكذا البحث عن معرفة أحوال القمر أهم المهمات. لأن الأسباب الأربعة المذكورة موجودة فيه:
فالأول: إن أقرب الكواكب إلى هذا العالم: القمر. وآثاره تصل إلى هذا العالم من غير واسطة. وأما آثار سائر الكواكب فإنها لا تصل إلى هذا العالم إلا بواسطة القمر. فوجب أن يكون البحث عن حال القمر، أهم من غيره.
والثاني: إن أحوال هذا العالم سريعة التغير والدوران. وأحوال القمر أيضاً كذلك.
والثالث: إن بسبب سرعة حركة القمر، تمتزج أنوار الكواكب بعضها ببعض، وبحسب تلك الامتزاجات تختلف حال الآثار الحاصلة في هذا العالم.
والرابع: إن أقوى الفاعلتين هو الحرارة، وأشد المنفعلتين استعداداً لقبول الأثر هو الرطوبة. ومتى لقي الفاعل القوي في التأثير المنفعل القوي في القبول: قوي الأثر، وكمل الفعل. فلهذا السبب كان الموجب لحدوث الكائنات تأثير الحرارة في الرطوبة. وينبوع الحرارة هو الشمس. وينبوع الرطوبة هو القمر. فكان الشمس كالأب. والقمر كالأم. وعند اجتماعهما تحدث المواليد. وأما سائر الكواكب فهي كالأعوان. فلهذا السبب وجب الاعتناء بمعرفة أحوال النيرين.
The influence, and it is indicated by aspects: First: They (the planets) are closer to this world than those fixed stars. Second: The fixed stars, as their name indicates, are fixed. So it is not fitting for them to be causes for these events which are rapidly changing in this world. Third: The fixed stars do not change their relative positions, neither in longitude nor in latitude, because they are embedded in one sphere, unlike the planets, for each of them is embedded in another sphere and each sphere has its own motion. So the motions of their spheres are in longitudes and latitudes, resulting in the different relationships that can be the principles of the occurrence of events in this world. Fourth: These planets pass by those fixed stars, and in this way the lights of some of those fixed stars mix with others. So it is established by this way that the most important in the world of stars is knowledge of the natures of the planets, then after that knowledge of the natures of the fixed stars. And know that just as research into the natures of the planets is more important than research into the natures of the fixed stars, so too research into knowledge of the states of the moon is the most important of important matters. Because the four mentioned causes exist in it: First: The closest planet to this world is the moon, and its effects reach this world without intermediary. As for the effects of other planets, they do not reach this world except through the moon. So it is necessary that research into the condition of the moon is more important than others. Second: The states of this world are rapidly changing and rotating, and the states of the moon are also likewise. Third: Because of the speed of the moon's motion, the lights of the planets mix with each other, and according to those mixtures the condition of the effects occurring in this world differ. Fourth: The strongest of the two active principles is heat, and the most receptive of the two passive principles in readiness to receive the effect is moisture. When the active principle strong in effect meets the passive principle strong in reception, the effect is strengthened and the action is perfected. For this reason, the cause of the generation of beings is the effect of heat upon moisture. The source of heat is the sun, and the source of moisture is the moon. So the sun is like the father, and the moon is like the mother, and when they come together, offspring occur. As for other planets, they are like assistants. For this reason, attention to knowledge of the states of the two luminaries is necessary.
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage presents a structured argument for why the moon is the most important celestial body to study in astrology/cosmology. The author begins by establishing that planets (al-sayyārāt) are more important than fixed stars (al-thawābit) using four reasons: proximity, suitability as causes for changing events, variability in relative positions enabling diverse effects, and mixing of lights. Then he applies the same four criteria to the moon, showing it surpasses other planets. The argument follows: (1) the moon is the closest planet, its effects reach earth directly while others require the moon as intermediary; (2) the moon’s rapid change mirrors earthly change; (3) its fast motion causes light mixtures affecting earthly phenomena; (4) heat (sun) and moisture (moon) are the primary active and passive principles generating beings, making the sun and moon like father and mother of generation. Therefore, studying the two luminaries (al-nayyirayn) is essential.

Key Terms
الثوابت
السيارات
التأثير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Fixed stars are more important because they are numerous and bright.
Correction: The author argues that planets' mutability and proximity make them more causally relevant despite fixed stars' numbers.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why are fixed stars not suitable causes for changing earthly events?
A) Because they are too far away.
B) Because they are fixed and unchanging by nature.
C) Because they do not mix their lights.
D) Because they are not mentioned in the Quran.

Key Takeaway
Planets are causally superior to fixed stars due to their proximity, suitability for change, variable positions, and light-mixing effects.

?
The author argues that what is closer and more directly involved in change is more important. How does this apply to your relationship with the world around you? Are you more focused on distant, fixed ideals or the immediate, changeable situations right in front of you?

Why the Moon is the Most Important Celestial Body
The author uses four criteria to argue that the moon is the most important planet to study.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the moon, among all planets, is the most important celestial body to study, based on the four criteria of causal relevance.

Core Idea
The moon’s proximity, rapid change, light-mixing, and role as source of moisture make it the key to earthly generation.

After establishing that planets as a group outrank fixed stars in causal importance, the author now focuses on the moon. Applying the same four criteria, he demonstrates that the moon surpasses all other planets. Moreover, he presents a striking analogy of the sun and moon as father and mother, with heat and moisture as the primary principles of generation. This lesson unpacks these arguments.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the moon's importance
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Notice how the author applies the four criteria already introduced.
The four criteria are: proximity, changeability, light mixing, and the heat-moisture principle.
2
Understand the first criterion applied to the moon
The moon is the closest planet, and its effects reach directly without intermediary. All other planets affect us only through the moon.
This establishes the moon's unique mediating role.
3
Understand the second and third criteria
The moon's rapid change mirrors earthly change, and its fast motion mixes the lights of other planets, causing variation in effects.
These criteria reinforce the moon's central role in generating diversity.
4
Understand the fourth criterion: the heat-moisture analogy
The sun (heat) and moon (moisture) are the primary active and passive principles; their interaction generates all beings. The moon is the source of moisture.
The sun is like father, moon like mother.

The influence, and it is indicated by aspects: First: They (the planets) are closer to this world than those fixed stars. Second: The fixed stars, as their name indicates, are fixed. So it is not fitting for them to be causes for these events which are rapidly changing in this world. Because the four mentioned causes exist in it: First: The closest planet to this world is the moon, and its effects reach this world without intermediary. As for the effects of other planets, they do not reach this world except through the moon. So it is necessary that research into the condition of the moon is more important than others. Second: The states of this world are rapidly changing and rotating, and the states of the moon are also likewise. Third: Because of the speed of the moon's motion, the lights of the planets mix with each other, and according to those mixtures the condition of the effects occurring in this world differ. Fourth: The strongest of the two active principles is heat, and the most receptive of the two passive principles in readiness to receive the effect is moisture. When the active principle strong in effect meets the passive principle strong in reception, the effect is strengthened and the action is perfected. For this reason, the cause of the generation of beings is the effect of heat upon moisture. The source of heat is the sun, and the source of moisture is the moon. So the sun is like the father, and the moon is like the mother, and when they come together, offspring occur. As for other planets, they are like assistants. For this reason, attention to knowledge of the states of the two luminaries is necessary.
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage presents a structured argument for why the moon is the most important celestial body to study in astrology/cosmology. The author begins by establishing that planets (al-sayyārāt) are more important than fixed stars (al-thawābit) using four reasons: proximity, suitability as causes for changing events, variability in relative positions enabling diverse effects, and mixing of lights. Then he applies the same four criteria to the moon, showing it surpasses other planets. The argument follows: (1) the moon is the closest planet, its effects reach earth directly while others require the moon as intermediary; (2) the moon’s rapid change mirrors earthly change; (3) its fast motion causes light mixtures affecting earthly phenomena; (4) heat (sun) and moisture (moon) are the primary active and passive principles generating beings, making the sun and moon like father and mother of generation. Therefore, studying the two luminaries (al-nayyirayn) is essential.

الشمس
النيرين

Correction: The author argues that both heat (sun) and moisture (moon) are necessary; the moon is the source of moisture, making it equally important.

Four Confirmations of the Sun and Moon's Significance
Four additional proofs for the sun and moon's importance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand four distinct reasons why classical scholars emphasized the sun and moon over other celestial bodies.

Core Idea
The sun and moon govern time, astrology, medicine, and tides unlike any other planets.

The author has already established the importance of the sun and moon. Now he provides four additional confirmations (wujūh ukhrā) that reinforce their unique roles. These proofs range from the division of day and night to medical and tidal influences, demonstrating that the sun and moon are not just lights but active agents in the world.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without pausing. Then read the translation. Notice the structure: 'Then... confirmed by other aspects: First... Second... Third... Fourth...'
The text cuts off at the end of the fourth point; the argument is complete in its current form.
2
Identify each of the four proofs
List the four proofs: (1) rulers of day and night, (2) astrological agreement on conjunction/opposition, (3) medical and tidal effects, (4) astronomical connection between moon and sun.
Each proof is introduced with a number (الأول, الثاني, etc.).
3
Understand the practical implications
Notice that these proofs are not theoretical; they involve observable phenomena like tides, vapors, and visibility of the moon.
This shows the sun and moon were considered causally influential in various sciences.
4
Answer the checkpoint question
Use the passage to answer the multiple-choice question about the moon's connection to the sun.

Commentary
This passage provides four additional confirmations (wujūh ukhrā) to reinforce the importance of studying the sun and moon (al-nayyirayn). First, they are the rulers of day and night, dividing time. Second, astrologers agree that the ascendant (ṭāli‘) of opposition (istiqbāl) and conjunction (ijtimā‘) of the sun and moon greatly affects the world, unlike other planets. Third, physicians attribute the distribution of vapors (bukhrānāt) and the tides (maddu wal-jazr) to the moon’s motion, indicating its practical influence. Fourth, the moon is strongly connected to the sun: their astrological houses are linked, and the moon’s visibility depends on separation from the sun. The text ends while explaining the calculation of the moon’s exaltation degree, indicating a continuation.

The Moon's Motion and Mixing of Lights
Razi's third proof: moon's motion mixes lights.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's third proof that the moon's rapid motion causes the mixing of planetary lights, leading to diverse effects in this world.

Core Idea
The moon's speed mixes lights, causing earthly variety.

Razi presents the moon's motion as a key factor in earthly diversity. By understanding how the moon's speed mixes the lights of other planets, we grasp why the moon is so important. This short proof highlights a celestial mechanism behind sublunar variation.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof slowly
Read the Arabic and translation, noting that the proof is a single causal statement: the moon's speed causes mixing of lights, which leads to differing effects.
2
Identify the causal chain
Break down the causal chain: moon's speed → mixing of planetary lights → variation in earthly effects. Each link is necessary.
3
Reflect on the implication
Consider why the moon's motion is singled out. This proof shows that the moon, despite being smaller, plays a active role in shaping earthly phenomena through its motion.
The sun is not mentioned here; the moon is the focus.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والثالث : إن بسبب سرعة حركة القمر ، تمتزج أنوار الكواكب بعضها بالبحر وبحسب تلك الامتزاجات تختلف حال الآثار الحاصلة في هذا العالم والرابع : إن أقوى الفاعلتين هو الحرارة ، وأشد المنفعلتين استعداداً لقبول الأثر هو الرطوبة . ومتى لقي الفاعل القوي في التأثير المنفعل القوي في القبول : قوي الأثر ، وكمل الفعل . فلهذا السبب كان الموجب لحدوث الكائنات تأثير الحرارة في الرطوبة. وينبوع الحرارة هو الشمس . وينبوع الرطوبة هو القمر . فكان الشمس كالأب . والقمر كالأم . وعند اجتماعهما تحدث المواليد . وأما سائر الكواكب فهي كالأعوان . فلهذا السبب وجب الاعتناء بمعرفة أحوال النيرين .
And the third: because of the speed of the moon’s motion, the lights of the planets mix with each other, and according to those mixtures the states of the effects occurring in this world differ. When strong heat acts on strong moisture, the effect is powerful and generation occurs. Since the sun is the source of heat and the moon the source of moisture, their conjunction produces all generated beings. The other planets are merely assistants. Therefore, knowledge of the sun and moon is essential.

Heat and Moisture: The Primary Agents of Generation
Razi's fourth proof: heat and moisture as primary causes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's fourth proof that the sun (heat) and moon (moisture) are the primary causes of generation in the sublunar world.

Core Idea
Sun as father (heat), moon as mother (moisture) – together they generate all beings.

Razi deepens the argument by identifying the most fundamental qualities: heat and moisture. He explains why the sun and moon are the sources of these qualities and compares them to parents. This proof establishes their unique and essential role in generation, with other planets as mere assistants.

Guided Path
1
Read the full argument

This is a longer argument than the third proof.

3
Understand the analogy
The sun is like a father (providing heat/action), the moon like a mother (providing moisture/receptivity). Their conjunction produces offspring (generated beings).
4
Consider the role of other planets
Other planets are called 'assistants', meaning they contribute but are not primary. This further elevates the sun and moon.
This addresses a potential objection: why only two luminaries?

Five Proofs for the Importance of the Sun and Moon
Razi enumerates five additional proofs for the importance of the sun and moon.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand five additional arguments from Fakhr al-Din al-Razi that demonstrate the unique and influential roles of the sun and moon compared to other celestial bodies.

Core Idea
The sun and moon are uniquely important due to their roles in day/night, astrology, medicine, tides, and apparent size.

Razi continues his case for the unique importance of the two luminaries by offering five arguments drawn from diverse fields: time division, astrology, medicine, celestial correlations, and visual perception. These proofs show how the sun and moon affect worldly phenomena in ways other celestial bodies do not. As you read, notice how each proof appeals to a different area of knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the structure
The passage lists five separate proofs. Each proof is introduced with 'the first', 'the second', etc. Read through all five to get an overview, then study each one carefully.
Razi uses enumeration to organize his arguments, making them easy to follow.
2
Examine Proof 1: Rulers of Day and Night
The first proof divides time into night and day, with the moon ruling night and the sun ruling day. This covers all of time, giving the two luminaries a universal domain.
3
Examine Proofs 2 and 3: Astrology and Medicine
The second proof notes that astrologers only consider conjunctions and oppositions of the sun and moon, not other planets. The third proof cites physicians who use the moon's motion for fumigations and tidal patterns.
These proofs rely on accepted practices in astrology and medicine.
4
Examine Proofs 4 and 5: Celestial Similarity
The fourth proof shows the moon's house and exaltation are connected to the sun's, and the fifth proof notes their similar apparent size. These suggest a special relationship and importance.
Reflect on how these arguments strengthen the case for the sun and moon's uniqueness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم تؤكد ما ذكرناه بوجوه أخرى : الأول : إن سلطان النهار : الشمس . وسلطان الليل : القمر . والزمان ينقسم إلى هذين القسمين : الليل والنهار . والثاني : إنهم أجمعوا على أن تطالع الاستقبال والاجتماع اثراً عظيماً في أحوال هذا العالم ، ولم يعتبروا أحوال الاجتماع والاستقبال في سائر الكواكب ، مثل ما اعتبروا في النيرين . والثالث : إن الأطباء أطبقوا على توزيع أمر البخرانات ، على أحوال حركة القمر . وعلى توزيع أحوال المد والجزر في البحار ، على أحوال حركة القمر . والرابع : إن القمر شديد الاتصال بالشمس. بدليل : أن بيته متصل ببيت الشمس ، وبيت شرفه متصل ببيت شرف الشمس ، بل قالوا : إن شرف الشمس في التاسع عشر من الحمل، والقمر إذا قارن الشمس ، فإنه لا يصير ممكن الرؤية ، إلا إذا تباعد عنها بمقدار اثنتي عشرة درجة . ولما كانت الدرجات قد تختلف مقاديرها ، بسبب اختلاف المطالع ، جعلوا درجة شرف القمر في الثالثة من الثور . وذلك يدل على مناسبة شديدة بينهما . والخامس : إنهما متشابهان في عظم الجرم، بحسب الحس .
Then we confirm what we mentioned with other aspects: The first: the ruler of the day is the sun, and the ruler of the night is the moon, and time is divided into these two divisions: night and day. The second: they all agree that the ascendants of opposition and conjunction have a great effect on the states of this world, and they did not consider the states of conjunction and opposition for the other planets as they did for the two luminaries. The third: the physicians unanimously prescribe the dosing of fumigations according to the states of the moon's motion, and the distribution of the states of ebb and flow in the seas according to the states of the moon's motion. The fourth: the moon is strongly connected to the sun, evidenced by the fact that its house is connected to the house of the sun, and its house of exaltation is connected to the house of the sun's exaltation; indeed they said that the sun's exaltation is in the 19th degree of Aries, and the moon, when it is in conjunction with the sun, cannot become visible until it separates from it by about twelve degrees. And since degrees may vary in magnitude due to differences in ascensions, they made the degree of the moon's exaltation in the third degree of Taurus. This indicates a strong similarity between them. And the fifth: they are similar in magnitude of body, according to sense perception.
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage enumerates five additional proofs for the special status of the sun and moon. The first proof: the sun rules day and the moon rules night, covering all of time. The second: astrologers universally agree that the conjunctions and oppositions of the sun and moon have great effects, but do not consider such aspects for other planets. The third: doctors rely on the moon's motion for timing fumigations, and the tides depend on the moon's motion. The fourth: the moon's house (Cancer) and exaltation (Taurus) are directly connected to the sun's house (Leo) and exaltation (Aries), and the interval of visibility after conjunction shows their close bond. The fifth: they appear similar in size to the eye. Together these prove the unique importance of the two luminaries.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: These proofs are based solely on Islamic revelation or pure reason.
Correction: The proofs are grounded in empirical observation (tides, visibility, size) and astrological/medical traditions, not revelation.

Astrological Correspondence and Zodiac Division
Astrologers explain their principle of similarity and divide the zodiac into houses and triplicities.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how astrologers use the principle of similarity to link celestial degrees to events and how they divide the zodiac into houses and triplicities.

Core Idea
Astrologers claim celestial degrees mirror terrestrial events, then split the zodiac into 12 houses and 4 triplicities.

Before refuting astrological claims, kalam scholars first present them clearly. This passage explains the core astrological concept of correspondence: a rising degree is taken as a sign for a newborn because both appear after concealment. It then describes two foundational divisions of the zodiac: into twelve houses and into four triplicities.

Guided Path
1
Read the astrological example
Read the first part of the passage describing the newborn child and the rising degree. Notice how they use the concept of 'appearing after concealment' to assert a similarity.
This similarity (mushābaha) is the basis for astrological inference.
2
Identify the division into houses
After the example, the passage states that astrologers divide the zodiacal circuit from that point into twelve sections called houses (buyūt). Find this statement in the Arabic.
These houses are part of the ascendant figure (ṭāliʿ).
3
Identify the division into triplicities
The passage then mentions a 'third division' into four triplicities: fire, earth, air, water. Locate these terms in the Arabic.
The text does not explain the first two divisions, only the third.
4
Reflect on the overall principle
Consider how the principle of similarity ties the example and the divisions together. Astrologers use this to claim that celestial configurations indicate earthly outcomes.
Later lessons will critique this reasoning from a kalam perspective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يظهر بعد الخفاء ، كالولد الذي ينفصل عن بطن الأم ، لابد وأن يطلع في تلك اللحظة درجة معينة من الفلك . فتلك الدرجة لما ظهرت بعد الخفاء ، كانت مشابهة لأحوال ذلك الولد الذي ظهر بعد الخفاء ، فجعلوا تلك الدرجة دليلاً على أحوال ذلك الحادث، ثم قسموا أدوار الفلك من تلك النقطة بأثني عشر قسماً . وهي البيوت الموجودة في صورة الطالع . والقسم الثالث (۱) : أنهم قسموا الفلك إلى المثلثات الأربعة وهي المثلثة : النارية والأرضية والهوائية والمائية .
It appears after concealment, like the child who separates from the womb of the mother: it is necessary that at that moment a specific degree of the zodiac rises. So that degree, when it appeared after concealment, was similar to the circumstances of that child who appeared after concealment. So they made that degree a proof of the circumstances of that event. Then they divided the circuits of the zodiac from that point into twelve sections. These are the houses present in the image of the ascendant. And the third division (1): that they divided the zodiac into four triplicities, which are the triplicities: fire, earth, air, and water.
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage is an exposition of the astrological principle of correspondence between celestial and terrestrial events. It begins with an example: a child emerging from the womb; at that moment a specific degree of the zodiac is rising. Because that degree appears after being hidden, it is considered similar to the child's emergence from concealment. Hence astrologers take that degree as an indicator (dalil) of the event. Then they divide the zodiacal cycle from that point into twelve sections called houses (buyut), which are the houses in the ascendant figure. Next, the author mentions the third division (al-qism al-thalith), which divides the zodiac into four triplicities (muthallathat): fire, earth, air, and water. The passage does not explain the first two divisions, but presents this as part of astrological theory.

The Twelve Subdivisions of Each Zodiac Sign
The text enumerates twelve types of subdivisions of each zodiac sign.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the twelve types of subdivisions of each zodiac sign as enumerated in the text, and specifically note the special role of lunar mansions in magical compositions.

Core Idea
Twelve ways to divide a zodiac sign.

This passage lists the third type of astrological division: subdividing each zodiac sign into twelve different categories. While most are simply named, the lunar mansions are highlighted for their powerful role in magical workings. Understanding these divisions is key to grasping the complex system of classical astrology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation, noting the twelve aspects.
The passage begins with 'والنوع الثالث' indicating this is the third type of division.
2
Identify the first division
Notice the lunar mansions and the remark about their strong power in composing magical works.
The text explicitly says 'لأن لها قوة شديدة في تركيب الأعمال السحرية'.
3
Review the remaining eleven divisions
Observe that most are just named without elaboration, from 'بيوت الكواكب' to 'الأقسام المذكرة والمؤنثة'.
Only the first and fourth (hudud) have brief descriptions.
4
Consider the significance
Think about why these divisions are categorized under the 'third type' and how they relate to astrological practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والنوع الثالث : قسمة كل برج إلى أقسام كثيرة . وهذا يقع على وجوه : الأول : قسمة البروج على منازل القمر .. ويجب البحث عن خاصية كل واحد من تلك المنازل . لأن لها قوة شديدة في تركيب الأعمال السحرية والثاني : معرفة بيوت الكواكب . والثالث : معرفة أشراف الكواكب . والرابع : الحدود، وهي قسمة كل برج بأقسام معينة ، وتخصيص كل واحد منها بكوكب معين . والخامس : الوجوه . والسادس : الذريحانات . والسابع : الاثنا عشريات . والثامن : النهبهرات . والتاسع : المفرح . العاشر : الحيز . والحادي عشر : الدستورية . والثاني عشر : الأقسام المذكرة والمؤنثة (۳)
And the third type: the division of each sign into many sections. This occurs in aspects: the first: the division of signs according to the lunar mansions. And one must investigate the property of each of those mansions, because they have strong power in composing magical works. The second: knowing the houses of the planets. The third: knowing the exaltations of the planets. The fourth: the terms, which is the division of each sign into specific sections, and the allocation of each one to a specific planet. The fifth: the faces. The sixth: the decans. The seventh: the duodecimae. The eighth: the nonths. The ninth: the joyful. The tenth: the space. The eleventh: the divisional. The twelfth: the masculine and feminine divisions.
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage presents the third type of astrological division: dividing each zodiac sign into many sections, which occurs in twelve aspects (wujuh). The first aspect is the division according to lunar mansions (manazil al-qamar); the text notes that one must investigate the property of each mansion because they have strong power in composing magical works. The second is knowing the houses of planets (buyut al-kawakib). The third is knowing the exaltations (ashraf) of planets. The fourth is the terms (hudud), where each sign is divided into certain sections, each assigned to a specific planet. The fifth is the faces (wujuh). The sixth is the decans (dharaihanat). The seventh is the duodecimae (ithna 'ashariyat). The eighth is the nonths (nuhbaharat). The ninth is the joyful (mufarrah). The tenth is the space (hayz). The eleventh is the divisional (dusturiyya). The twelfth is the masculine and feminine divisions (al-aqsam al-mudhakkarah wa al-mu'annathah). The list covers common astrological subdivisions, though the precise identification of some terms may vary.

The Fourth Division: Thirty Degrees and Three Ancient Narrations
Enumerates the fourth division and three ancient narrations on degree properties.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the fourth type of astrological division (thirty degrees per sign) and the three ancient traditions that assign properties, names, incense, and effects to each degree.

Core Idea
The zodiac is further divided into 30 degrees, each with unique properties from ancient sages.

In this passage, the author presents yet another layer of astrological detail: the division of each sign into 30 individual degrees. He then cites three different ancient sources—Indian, Persian, and Babylonian—that attribute specific natures, effects, and rituals to each degree. This shows the cross-cultural interest in micro-astrology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without stopping. Then read the translation to grasp the overall meaning.
Notice the enumeration of three narrations.
2
Identify the three narrations
Find each narration: Tamtam al-Hindi, Zardusht (Zoroaster), and the Babylonians. Note what each is said to provide (properties, names, incense, etc.).
The first narration includes a specific ritual.
3
Reflect on the ritual
Consider the prescribed action when the sun enters a degree: burning incense, calling upon the degree's lord by name, and requesting its effect. Think about how this reflects a belief in astrological causation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والنوع الرابع : قسمة البروج إلى ثلاثين درجة . ومعرفة طبائع تلك الدرجات وآثارها وكيفياتها . وللقدماء فيها روايات : . إحداها : ما يروى عن طمطم الهندي ) فإنه يذكر لكل درجة خاصيتها وأسماءها وبخورها وأثرها . فإذا نزلت الشمس في تلك الدرجة ، وجب التبخير ، بذلك البخور ، ودعا صاحب تلك الدرجة بذلك الاسم ، وطلب ذلك الأثر منه . والرواية الثانية : خواص تلك الدرجات [ بحسب ما هو منقول عن و زردشت ) . والرواية الثالثة : خواصها (۱) ] بحسب ما هو منقول عن البابليين (۱) من (ل) .
And the fourth type: the division of signs into thirty degrees. And knowing the natures of those degrees, their effects, and their qualities. And the ancients have narrations concerning them. One of them: what is narrated from Tamtam al-Hindi, for he mentioned for each degree its property, its names, its incense, and its effect. So when the sun descends into that degree, it is obligatory to fumigate with that incense, and to call upon the lord of that degree by that name, and to request that effect from him. The second narration: the properties of those degrees according to what is transmitted from Zardusht (Zoroaster). The third narration: their properties according to what is transmitted from the Babylonians.
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage describes the fourth type of astrological division: dividing the zodiac into thirty degrees, and knowing the natures (taba'i'), effects (athar), and qualities (kayfiyyat) of those degrees. It then cites three ancient narrations (riwayat) about the degrees. The first narration is from Tamtam al-Hindi (the Indian), who assigned to each degree its property (khassiyya), names (asma'), incense (bakhur), and effect (athar). The text describes a ritual: when the sun enters that degree, one must fumigate with the specified incense, call upon the 'lord' (sahib) of that degree by its name, and request the desired effect from him. The second narration is from Zardusht (Zoroaster), the Persian founder of Zoroastrianism. The third narration is from the Babylonians. Thus, the passage presents astrological degree lore as derived from multiple ancient cultures.

The Rationale for the Qualities of Cardinal Signs
Al-Razi explains the rationale for the hot/cold/dry/wet qualities of the four cardinal signs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why al-Razi assigns specific hot/cold/dry/wet qualities to the four cardinal signs based on the principles of alternating active qualities and pairing passive ones.

Core Idea
The world's survival requires alternating active qualities and pairing passive ones.

Al-Razi explains the qualities of the cardinal signs not as arbitrary but as necessary for cosmic balance. He shows how the sun's transitions and the nature of active/passive qualities determine the pattern. This passage reveals the rational structure underlying astrological attributions in classical Islamic thought.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the transition from specific example to general principle.
2
Identify the sun's transition points
Note how the sun's movement from Gemini to Cancer (descent) and from Sagittarius to Capricorn (ascent) is used to explain the qualities of Cancer and Capricorn.
This establishes the empirical basis.
3
Understand active vs passive qualities
Al-Razi distinguishes between heat/cold (active, strong) and dryness/wetness (passive, weak). Grasp why this distinction matters for the overall argument.
Active qualities are strong; passive are weak.
4
Follow the alternating rule for actives
Why must hot and cold signs alternate? Because if two hot or two cold were consecutive, the effect would be too great and destroy the world.
This is a teleological argument.
5
Follow the pairing rule for passives
Why should dry and wet occur in pairs? Because if they alternated, they would moderate each other's effects and nullify them. So two dry then two wet is superior.
This leads to the pattern of four signs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
انتقال الشمس من الجوزاء إلى السرطان، تأخذ في الهبوط ، ونقصان النهار ، وزيادة الليل ، وعند الانتقال من القوس إلى الجدي، تنتقل الشمس من الهبوط إلى الصعود ، ومن غاية انتقاص النهار إلى ازدياده . فالجدي أفضل من السرطان. فلهذا جعلوا الجدي بارداً يابساً . والسرطان بارداً رطباً . فصارت طبائع هذه البروج الأربعة : معلومة

ثم نقول : الحرارة والبرودة فاعلتان . واليبوسة والرطوبة منفعلتان . والفاعل قوي ، والمنفعل ضعيف ، فلو توالى حاران ، أو باردان ، لعظم التسخين أو التبريد ، ولهلك العالم . فوجب أن يحصل برج حار ، ثم برج بارد ، ثم حار ، ثم بارد ، وأما المنفعلتان ، فلو حصل يابس ثم رطب ، لاعتدل كل واحد منهما بالآخر ، ولبطل تأثير كل واحد منها ، فالأصوب أن يحصل يابان ، ثم رطبان . وهكذا على الترتيب . وإذا ظهرت هذه المقدمات ، وجب أن يكون الأول حاراً يابساً ، والثاني بارد يابساً ، والثالث حاراً رطباً، والرابع بارداً رطباً . وكذا القول في الأربعة الثانية والثالثة.
Transition of the sun from Gemini to Cancer: it takes in descent, decrease of daytime, and increase of night; and at the transition from Sagittarius to Capricorn, the sun moves from descent to ascent, and from the extreme of decrease of daytime to its increase. So Capricorn is better than Cancer. For this reason they made Capricorn cold-dry (bārid yābis), and Cancer cold-wet (bārid ratb). So the natures of these four signs became known. Then we say: Heat and cold (al-ḥarāra wa al-burūda) are active (fāʿilatān). Dryness and wetness (al-yubūsa wa al-ruṭūba) are passive (munfaʿilatān). The active is strong, and the passive is weak. If two hot or two cold [signs] were consecutive, the heating or cooling would be great and the world would perish. So it is necessary that a hot sign occur, then a cold one, then hot, then cold. As for the two passive [qualities], if dry occurred then wet, each would be moderated by the other and the effect of each would be nullified. So the most correct is that two dry [signs] occur, then two wet. And so on in order. When these premises are established, it must be that the first is hot-dry, the second cold-dry, the third hot-wet, and the fourth cold-wet. And the same applies to the second and third quadruplicities.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage defines the rationale for the qualities of the four cardinal signs (Aries, Cancer, Libra, Capricorn). The author begins by describing the sun's transition points causing the change of seasons. He then argues that the active qualities (heat and cold) must alternate to prevent destruction, while the passive qualities (dryness and wetness) should occur in pairs to nullify each other's extreme effects. This results in the first sign (Aries) being hot-dry, second (Cancer) cold-wet, third (Libra) hot-wet, fourth (Capricorn) cold-dry. He says the same applies to the second and third quadruplicities (the fixed and mutable signs). The reasoning is based on the principle that the world's survival requires balance in active and passive qualities.

Key Terms
الحرارة والبرودة (heat and cold)
اليبوسة والرطوبة (dryness and wetness)
فاعلتان (active)
منفعلتان (passive)
البروج (signs)
الهبوط (descent)
الصعود (ascent)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The qualities of the signs are arbitrary or based solely on observation.
Correction: Al-Razi shows they are derived from rational principles of balance between active and passive qualities, necessary for the world's survival.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The qualities of the cardinal signs are determined by the necessity of alternating active qualities and pairing passive ones to maintain cosmic balance.

The Three Ranks of Opposite Things
Classification of opposite things into three ranks based on qualitative opposition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the classification of opposite things into three ranks based on which qualities are in opposition.

Core Idea
Opposites differ not just in degree but in which qualities are opposed.

The author now turns from the general principle of similarity to the classification of opposites. He identifies three ranks of opposition, distinguished by whether the conflict involves both active and passive qualities or only passive ones. This classification is then applied to planets and medicines.

Guided Path
1
Read the classification of ranks
Read the Arabic passage carefully, noting the three ranks described. Pay attention to the example given for the first rank.
The third rank is described identically to the second in the text, which may indicate a textual issue.
2
Compare the second and third ranks
Notice that both the second and third ranks are defined as opposition only in the two passive qualities. Consider why the author might have repeated this or what subtle distinction might be intended.
3
Consider the application
Read the instruction to apply these states to planets and medicines. Reflect on how the qualitative composition of celestial bodies and substances determines their interactions.
This links the abstract classification to practical astrology and medicine.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الأشياء المضادة. فهي أيضاً على ثلاث مراتب. فالمرتبة الأولى: أن يكون التنافي حاصلاً في الكيفيتين معاً. مثل: الحار اليابس مع البارد الرطب. والمرتبة الثانية - وهي المتوسطة - أن يكون التنافي حاصلاً في الكيفيتين المنفعلتين فقط. والمرتبة الثالثة - وهي الأخيرة - أن يكون التنافي حاصلاً في الكيفيتين المنفعلتين فقط. وإذا عرفت هذا، فيجب أن تعتبر هذه الأحوال في الكواكب وفي الأدوية. وأما اعتبار المشاكلة في الفلكيات. فنقول: المشاكلة التامة حاصلة بالتثليث، وهو الأول والخامس والتاسع. لأن البروج المتناظرة بحسب التثليث تكون متشاكلة في الكيفيتين معاً. مثل الحمل والأسد والقوس، إلا أن أقواها هو الأوسط، وهو الأسد، ثم الأخير وهو القوس، ثم الأول وهو الحمل. وإذا عرفت الحال في هذا المثال، فقس البواقي عليه.
As for opposite things, they too are of three ranks. The first rank: that opposition occurs in both qualities together, such as hot-dry with cold-wet. The second rank—which is intermediate—that opposition occurs only in the two passive qualities. The third rank—which is the last—that opposition occurs only in the two passive qualities. And when you know this, you must consider these states in the planets and in medicines. As for the consideration of similarity in celestial things, we say: complete similarity is achieved by triplicity, which is the first, fifth, and ninth. For the signs that correspond according to triplicity are similar in both qualities together, such as Aries, Leo, and Sagittarius, except that the strongest of them is the middle, Leo, then the last, Sagittarius, then the first, Aries. And when you understand the case in this example, analogize the rest to it.
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage classifies opposite things into three ranks based on the qualities they involve. The first rank has opposition in both active and passive qualities together (e.g., hot-dry vs. cold-wet). The second rank has opposition only in the two passive qualities. The third rank also has opposition only in the two passive qualities, but the author does not specify a difference between second and third here—perhaps a textual issue or a later distinction. The author then applies these states to planets and medicines. Next, he explains the concept of 'complete similarity' in celestial matters, which is achieved by triplicity—the aspects of 1st, 5th, and 9th signs. Signs in these positions share both qualities. For example, Aries, Leo, and Sagittarius are all hot and dry? Actually, the text says they are similar in both qualities together. The strongest is the middle sign (Leo), then the last, then the first. The reader is instructed to analogize to other triplicities.

Key Terms
أشياء مضادة
كيفيتان
تنافي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The three ranks are simply about hot vs cold or similar binaries.
Correction: The ranks are about which qualities—active and passive—are in opposition, not just the degree of opposition.

Checkpoint

C) Only the active qualities

Key Takeaway
Opposite things are classified into three ranks based on whether the opposition involves both qualities or only the passive ones.

Triplicity and Celestial Similarity
Explanation of triplicity as the basis for complete similarity in celestial bodies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the concept of triplicity determines complete similarity among zodiac signs based on shared qualities.

Core Idea
Complete similarity among signs is achieved through triplicity—the first, fifth, and ninth signs.

Having established the ranks of opposites, the author now applies the principle of similarity to the celestial sphere. He explains that certain signs form a triplicity, sharing both qualities in common, with one sign being strongest. This forms the basis for astrological judgments based on sign positions.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of triplicity
Read the Arabic passage and note that complete similarity is achieved by triplicity, which is defined as the first, fifth, and ninth positions.
2
Examine the example
The example given is Aries, Leo, and Sagittarius. Understand that these share both qualities (e.g., hot and dry). Identify which is the strongest according to the text.
The strongest is the middle sign (Leo), then the last (Sagittarius), then the first (Aries).
3
Apply the principle
The author instructs to analogize to other triplicities. Consider how this pattern would apply to other elemental groups (e.g., earth, air, water).
This principle is used in astrological interpretations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الأشياء المضادة. فهي أيضاً على ثلاث مراتب. فالمرتبة الأولى: أن يكون التنافي حاصلاً في الكيفيتين معاً. مثل: الحار اليابس مع البارد الرطب. والمرتبة الثانية - وهي المتوسطة - أن يكون التنافي حاصلاً في الكيفيتين المنفعلتين فقط. والمرتبة الثالثة - وهي الأخيرة - أن يكون التنافي حاصلاً في الكيفيتين المنفعلتين فقط. وإذا عرفت هذا، فيجب أن تعتبر هذه الأحوال في الكواكب وفي الأدوية. وأما اعتبار المشاكلة في الفلكيات. فنقول: المشاكلة التامة حاصلة بالتثليث، وهو الأول والخامس والتاسع. لأن البروج المتناظرة بحسب التثليث تكون متشاكلة في الكيفيتين معاً. مثل الحمل والأسد والقوس، إلا أن أقواها هو الأوسط، وهو الأسد، ثم الأخير وهو القوس، ثم الأول وهو الحمل. وإذا عرفت الحال في هذا المثال، فقس البواقي عليه.
As for opposite things, they too are of three ranks. The first rank: that opposition occurs in both qualities together, such as hot-dry with cold-wet. The second rank—which is intermediate—that opposition occurs only in the two passive qualities. The third rank—which is the last—that opposition occurs only in the two passive qualities. And when you know this, you must consider these states in the planets and in medicines. As for the consideration of similarity in celestial things, we say: complete similarity is achieved by triplicity, which is the first, fifth, and ninth. For the signs that correspond according to triplicity are similar in both qualities together, such as Aries, Leo, and Sagittarius, except that the strongest of them is the middle, Leo, then the last, Sagittarius, then the first, Aries. And when you understand the case in this example, analogize the rest to it.
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage classifies opposite things into three ranks based on the qualities they involve. The first rank has opposition in both active and passive qualities together (e.g., hot-dry vs. cold-wet). The second rank has opposition only in the two passive qualities. The third rank also has opposition only in the two passive qualities, but the author does not specify a difference between second and third here—perhaps a textual issue or a later distinction. The author then applies these states to planets and medicines. Next, he explains the concept of 'complete similarity' in celestial matters, which is achieved by triplicity—the aspects of 1st, 5th, and 9th signs. Signs in these positions share both qualities. For example, Aries, Leo, and Sagittarius are all hot and dry? Actually, the text says they are similar in both qualities together. The strongest is the middle sign (Leo), then the last, then the first. The reader is instructed to analogize to other triplicities.

Misconception: Triplicity simply means any group of three signs.
Correction: Triplicity specifically refers to signs that are 1st, 5th, and 9th apart, sharing complete qualitative similarity.

Key Takeaway
Triplicity is the pattern of signs 1st, 5th, and 9th apart that share complete similarity in qualities, with the middle sign being strongest.
