Making Talismans: Focused Imagination and Celestial Forces
Description of making talismans to cause disease or heat, with theoretical basis.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the third type of practical operation—making talismans—and how it relies on focused imagination, psychic power, and celestial influences.

Core Idea
Talismans work by focusing the imagination and harnessing celestial and psychic forces.

This passage introduces the third type of practical operation in the chapter: making talismans. The author details specific actions for causing disease or heat using a statue, and then explains the underlying theory involving celestial influences and psychic power. It is a blend of physical ritual, mental concentration, and belief in cosmic causality.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its literal translation to understand the practical steps described.
The Arabic uses technical terms for materials and actions.
2
Identify the practical actions
Notice the two main purposes: inflicting disease or causing heat. The author gives specific methods: applying substances inside the head or on the heart, writing incantations on iron or paper.
These actions are performed on a statue (tamthāl).
3
Understand the mental preparation
The author emphasizes emptying the heart of other work and strengthening the imagination. The benefit of making the image is to gather thoughts and strengthen the imagination.
Mental focus is crucial for the operation's success.
4
Analyze the causal theory
The effect occurs when strong celestial influences combine with lower receptive bodies and strong psychic power. If the working soul has special strength and suitability, the effect reaches its utmost.
This reflects a worldview where celestial and psychic forces interact.
5
Reflect on the misconception
The passage clarifies that talismans are not purely magic but rely on focused intention and natural forces.
This guards against misunderstanding the practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النوع الثالث من الأمور المعتبرة في هذا الباب: وهو قريب مما تقدم: أنك إذا فرغت التمثال، فإذا أردت تسليط المرض على دماغه، طلبت داخل رأسه بالأفيون واليبروج. وإن أردت تسليط الحرارة عليه، طليت موضع قلبه بالأطلية الحارة المحرقة، أو كتبت العزيمة على حديدة، وألقيتها في النار، أو كتبت العزيمة على كاغد، وألقيته في القارورة. وإذا فعلت هذه الأمور تكلفت تفريغ القلب عن كل عمل سوى هذا العمل، وقويت ذلك الخيال في نفسك وتصورت حصول تلك الحالة في ذلك العضو من ذلك الإنسان. والفائدة في عمل تلك الصورة: جمع الأفكار، وتقوية الخيال. فإنه متى انضمت المؤثرات الفلكية القوية إلى جملة الأجسام القابلة السفلية، وانضم إليها القوة النفسانية القوية التامة: حصل ذلك الأمر لا محال، فإن انضم إلى تلك الثلاثة كون تلك النفس العاملة مخصوصة بمزيد قوة في هذا الباب، ومزيد مناسبة لتلك الأعمال، بلغت الغاية فيه.
The third type of matters considered in this chapter: it is close to what preceded: that when you finish the statue, if you want to inflict disease on its brain, you apply inside its head with opium and verjuice. And if you want to inflict heat on it, you apply on its heart with hot burning ointments, or you write the incantation on a piece of iron and throw it into the fire, or you write the incantation on paper and throw it into the vial. And when you do these things, you undertake to empty the heart of every work other than this work, and you strengthen that imagination in yourself and imagine the occurrence of that state in that organ of that person. The benefit of making that image is to gather thoughts and strengthen the imagination. For whenever strong celestial influences join the totality of lower receptive bodies, and strong complete psychic power joins them, that thing happens inevitably. And if to these three is added that the working soul is distinguished by additional strength in this chapter and additional suitability for those works, it reaches the utmost in it.
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage describes the third type of practical operation: making talismans. The author explains that after crafting an image (statue), one can cause disease in its brain by applying opium and verjuice inside its head, or cause heat by applying hot burning ointments to its heart. Alternatively, one can write an incantation on iron and throw it into fire, or on paper and throw it into a vial. The key is to empty the mind of all other thoughts and strongly imagine the desired effect on the person's organ. The benefit of making the image is to concentrate thoughts and strengthen the imagination. The author then gives the theoretical basis: when strong celestial influences combine with lower receptive bodies and strong psychic power, the effect occurs inevitably. If in addition the soul performing the act has special strength and suitability, the effect reaches its utmost intensity. This shows a belief in the power of imagination combined with celestial and psychic forces.

The Fourth Type: Incense and Planetary Herbs
Explanation of the fourth type: incense based on planetary correspondences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the role of planetary correspondences in the practice of incense as described in traditional astrological sciences.

Core Idea
Each planet has its own herbs—burn the right one for your purpose.

This lesson presents the fourth category of practices considered in this chapter: incense. The author explains that the use of incense is not arbitrary but is based on a well-established science of astrological correspondences, where each planet has specific herbs assigned to it. The practitioner must select the appropriate substances to achieve the desired effect.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the passage is concise and states a principle.
2
Understand planetary-herb correspondence
Identify the key claim: each wandering planet (كوكب سيار) has specific herbs (عقاقير) that belong to it. This is presented as established knowledge in the science of judgments (علم الأحكام).
The seven classical planets (Moon, Mercury, Venus, Sun, Mars, Jupiter, Saturn) are typically meant.
3
Apply the practical implication
The rule is: whoever wants to produce incense for a particular planet must burn those things that are suitable (مناسبة) for that planet. Reflect on how this principle guides the practice.
This is not about worship but about astrological operation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النوع الرابع من الأمور المعتبرة في هذا الباب: الدخن. ولما ثبت في علم الأحكام: أن لكل واحد من الكواكب السيارة أنواعاً من العقاقير مختصة به، فمن أراد إحداث الدخنة لأجله، وجب التدخين بتلك الأشياء المناسبة له.
The fourth type of matters considered in this chapter: incense. Since it is established in the science of judgments that each of the wandering planets has types of herbs specific to it, whoever wants to produce incense for its sake must burn those things that are suitable for it.
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage introduces the fourth type of practice: incense (dukhn). The author states that it is established in the science of astrological judgments (علم الأحكام) that each of the seven wandering planets (the classical planets including Moon, Sun, etc.) has specific types of herbs (عقاقير) that belong to it. Therefore, if one wants to make incense for a particular planet, one must burn those substances that are appropriate to that planet. This is a brief note on astrological correspondences.

Key Terms

Key Takeaway
Incense in this tradition is a precise practice based on planetary correspondences, not a random selection of scents.

The Fifth Type: Known Words in Recitations
Explanation of the first kind of recitations: known words and their effect through knowledge of planetary attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the mechanism by which known words in incantations (ruqa) derive their efficacy from knowledge of planetary attributes and the resulting spiritual attraction.

Core Idea
Known words in incantations gain power through the reciter's knowledge and the resulting spiritual impression.

In this passage, the author of al-Matalib al-Aliyah explains a key principle of incantation: the effectiveness of known words depends on the reciter's knowledge of the celestial bodies involved. This insight bridges cosmology and psychology, showing how the mind's engagement with the cosmos influences spiritual power. The passage presents a clear causal chain that you will explore step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic source passage once, then read the English translation. Notice the clear two-part structure: classification of recitations, then explanation of known words.
The author uses a conditional structure: 'the more... the more...'
2
Identify the two kinds of recitations
The passage begins by stating that recitations (ruqa) are of two kinds: known words and unknown words. Pause to understand this division before moving to the explanation of known words.
3
Analyze the causal chain for known words
The author presents a chain: knowledge of a planet's attributes → ability to enumerate its perfect attributes → impression on the soul → attraction to the planet's spirit → power to influence. Trace each step and see how each leads to the next.
This chain shows that the power does not lie in the words themselves but in the reciter's knowledge and resulting inner state.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النوع الخامس من الأمور المعتبرة في هذا الباب: قراءة الرقي. واعلم أنها على قسمين: منها: كلمات معلومة، ومنها: كلمات غير معلومة. أما الكلمات المعلومة. فالحق عندي: أن الإنسان كلما كان وقوفه على صفات الكوكب المعين أكثر، وعلمه بأفعاله المخصوصة أتم، كانت قدرته على إحصاء صفات كماله أتم، وانفعال نفسه عند ذكر تلك الصفات أتم وكلما كان ذلك الانفعال أكمل، كان انجذاب نفسه إلى روح ذلك الكوكب أكمل، فكانت قدرته على التأثير أقوى.
The fifth type of matters considered in this chapter: recitation of incantations. Know that they are of two kinds: some are known words, and some are unknown words. As for the known words, the truth in my view is that the more a person's knowledge of the attributes of a particular planet is extensive, and his knowledge of its specific actions is more complete, his ability to enumerate its attributes of perfection is more complete, and the impression on his soul when mentioning those attributes is more complete. And the more complete that impression is, the more complete is the attraction of his soul to the spirit of that planet, and thus his power to influence is stronger.
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage presents the fifth type of practice: recitation of incantations (ruqa). The author divides recitations into two kinds: known words (معلومة) and unknown words (غير معلومة). He then explains the effect of known words. His view is that the effectiveness depends on the reciter's knowledge. The more he knows the attributes and specific actions of a particular planet, the better he can enumerate its perfect attributes, and the stronger the impression on his soul when reciting them. This impression, in turn, attracts his soul to the spirit of that planet, increasing his power to influence. Thus, knowledge and emotional engagement enhance the efficacy of the recitation.

Key Terms

كلمات معلومة
كوكب
روح
انفعال
انجذاب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The power of known words in incantations comes from the words themselves or their inherent properties.
Correction: The passage teaches that the power comes from the reciter's knowledge of the planet and the resulting impression and attraction, not from the words alone.

Checkpoint

A) The length of the recitation
B) The knowledge of the planet's attributes and actions
C) The loudness of the voice
D) The number of times it is repeated

Key Takeaway
The effectiveness of known words in ruqa depends on the reciter's knowledge and the resulting spiritual impression that attracts the planet's spirit.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
